### Confidentiality & Disclaimer

This document contains proprietary information about the Cuboid business concept, including product architecture, go-to-market strategy (including grey-market dynamics), financial projections, and partner engagement models. The information contained herein is provided for evaluation purposes only and shall not be reproduced, distributed, or disclosed to any third party without the express written permission of the document owner.

**Acknowledgment of Market Realities:** This document discusses the role of informal FX brokers (including bank workers and grey-market operators) as primary movers in Nigerian retail FX. Cuboid does not endorse unlicensed FX trading. The platform is designed for licensed entities. However, understanding real-world workflows is essential to building a solution that can onboard informal players into compliance over time.

**Special Disclosure:** Insane Technologies holds a minimum of 25% equity in Cuboid. The funding requirement of **$5,500 (minimum)** is an overly discounted strategic round and does not reflect the venture's long-term valuation. This round is intended for hands-on partners who will actively contribute to product development, compliance setup, broker network access, or BDC relationships.

## SECTION 2: EXECUTIVE SUMMARY (BROKER-AWARE EDITION)

### 2.1 The Cuboid Concept in One Paragraph

Cuboid is a digital FX network built for the way foreign exchange actually moves in Nigeria today. The primary movers are not licensed BDCs alone but **informal FX brokers**—bank workers, treasury staff, and trusted middlemen—who source dollars through their relationships and sell to customers via WhatsApp, phone calls, and personal networks. These brokers move significant volume, their customers trust them deeply, and they operate entirely outside regulatory visibility. Cuboid does not seek to disrupt or replace them. Instead, Cuboid provides a **digital layer** that makes their existing workflow faster, more reliable, and optionally compliant. Licensed BDCs use Cuboid to digitize operations and trade amongst themselves. Brokers use Cuboid (informally, at their own discretion) to manage relationships, generate quotes, and settle faster—while Cuboid maintains regulatory defensibility by clearly positioning itself as a tool for licensed entities. Insane Technologies holds at least 25% equity. The minimum funding requirement is **$5,500** (an overly discounted strategic round).

### 2.2 The Real Primary Movers (What Most Documents Get Wrong)

Most fintech concept notes describe a tidy world where licensed BDCs receive FX from banks, sell to customers, and report to regulators. This is not reality.

**Reality:** The most efficient, most trusted, and highest-volume FX traders in Nigeria are **informal brokers**. They include:

- **Bank tellers and branch managers** who have daily access to dollar-denominated accounts and wholesale FX windows.  
- **Treasury officers** who know when their bank has excess USD and can allocate it quietly.  
- **Former bank workers** who maintained their relationships after leaving.  
- **Trusted individuals** with direct lines to corporate FX holders or parallel market sources.

**How they work:**

| Step | Current Method | Pain Point |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1\. Customer needs USD | Calls or WhatsApps a trusted broker | No rate transparency |
| 2\. Broker checks inventory | Calls 5–10 contacts, asks "any dollar?" | Slow, exhausting |
| 3\. Broker quotes rate | Mental math based on what they heard | Inconsistent pricing |
| 4\. Customer agrees | Verbal confirmation | No binding commitment |
| 5\. Settlement | Bank transfer or cash handover | Settlement risk, no dispute resolution |
| 6\. Record keeping | WhatsApp message or nothing | No audit trail, no repeat customer insights |

**Why this matters for Cuboid:** These brokers already have what Cuboid needs—trust, volume, and customer relationships. If Cuboid ignores them, Cuboid ignores the real engine of retail FX. If Cuboid openly endorses them, Cuboid faces regulatory backlash. The solution is to **build a platform that appeals to their workflow without legitimizing their unlicensed status**, and to create a **pathway for them to formalize** (partner with a BDC or get licensed) while using Cuboid.

### 2.3 The Problem in Brief (Corrected)

**For informal brokers (primary movers):**

- They waste hours daily calling contacts to find FX inventory.  
- They have no digital tool to track customer requests, quotes, or settlements.  
- They cannot scale beyond their personal network.  
- They face settlement risk (customer pays, broker fails to deliver—or vice versa).  
- They are invisible to regulators, which is both an advantage (no compliance burden) and a risk (one whistleblower could end their operation).

**For licensed BDCs:**

- They are losing market share to faster, more flexible informal brokers.  
- They have high compliance burdens that brokers avoid.  
- They cannot trade easily amongst themselves.  
- They lack digital tools to compete with brokers' WhatsApp-style speed.

**For regulators (CBN, NFIU):**

- They have no visibility into the majority of retail FX volume (which flows through informal brokers).  
- They cannot enforce compliance on players they cannot see.  
- They rely on licensed BDCs for data, but BDCs represent only a fraction of actual activity.

**For end customers:**

- They get dollars, but at unpredictable rates and with no receipt or recourse.  
- They trust their broker personally but have no protection if something goes wrong.

### 2.4 The Solution in Brief (Two-Layer)

Cuboid is built as a **single platform with two modes of engagement**—one for licensed entities, one for informal users that maintains regulatory defensibility.

**Layer 1: For Licensed BDCs (Formal, Compliant, Visible)**

- BDC Management Module (inventory, customer records, receipts, inter-BDC trading).  
- Automated CBN/NFIU reporting.  
- Real-time regulator dashboard (opt-in for regulators).  
- API access for fintechs and banks.

**Layer 2: For Informal Brokers (Discretionary, Unendorsed, but Appealing)**

- Cuboid does not market to brokers as a compliance solution. But the product *feels* like it was built for them.  
- **Chat-to-trade:** Type "need $5k" into a WhatsApp-like interface; Cuboid matches with available inventory from licensed BDCs (or other brokers who have opted into visibility).  
- **Quick quote generation:** Generate a professional-looking quote to send to a customer in seconds.  
- **Customer management:** Store customer requests, history, and preferences (optional, local-only, no cloud if they prefer).  
- **Settlement escrow (light):** Hold customer funds briefly while broker sources FX; release only when confirmed.  
- **Referral pathway:** Brokers who refer licensed BDCs to Cuboid earn a revenue share. Brokers who want to formalize can partner with a BDC on the platform or apply for their own license via a guided process.

**Crucially:** Cuboid's terms of service prohibit unlicensed FX trading. Brokers who use the platform for unlicensed activity do so against the terms. Cuboid maintains audit trails and can provide them to regulators if required. But the product design does not *prevent* brokers from using it—because preventing them would mean losing the volume and trust they bring.

### 2.5 Market Opportunity (Formal \+ Grey)

| Metric | Estimate | Notes |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Licensed BDCs in Nigeria | 5,000 – 5,800 | Formal, visible, compliance-burdened |
| Active informal FX brokers | 15,000 – 30,000 | Bank workers, former bank staff, trusted agents |
| Annual retail FX turnover (formal BDC channel) | $5B – $8B | Reported to CBN |
| Annual retail FX turnover (informal broker channel) | $10B – $20B (estimated) | Unreported, invisible |
| **Total addressable retail FX market** | **$15B – $28B** |  |
| Brokers using any digital tool today | \<1% | Mostly WhatsApp and phone |
| BDCs using any digital management tool | \~10% | Mostly Excel |
| Cuboid's target Year 2 (active users) | 500 BDCs \+ 5,000 brokers (informal) | Brokers as volume drivers |

**The insight:** The informal market is *larger* than the formal market. Cuboid's strategy is not to replace brokers but to become the digital layer they adopt voluntarily, while providing licensed BDCs with tools to compete and regulators with a pathway to visibility.

### 2.6 Business Model (Broker-Driven Volume)

Cuboid's revenue streams are designed to capture value from the volume that brokers already move.

| Revenue Stream | Mechanism | Target (Year 2\) |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **Transaction fees (broker-originated)** | 0.1% – 0.3% on trades facilitated via Cuboid (matched with licensed BDC inventory) | $2B volume → $2M – $6M |
| **BDC Management Module subscription** | $20 – $100 per month per licensed BDC | 500 BDCs → $120k – $600k ARR |
| **Broker referral fees** | Brokers who refer a BDC to Cuboid earn 10% of that BDC's subscription for 12 months | Converts brokers into sales channel |
| **Compliance-as-a-Service (BDCs only)** | $10 – $30 per month for automated CBN/NFIU filing | 500 BDCs → $60k – $180k ARR |
| **API access (fintechs, banks)** | Tiered pricing for programmatic FX integration | 5 partners → $50k – $200k ARR |
| **Inter-BDC trading spread** | 0.05% – 0.1% on peer-to-peer BDC trades | $500M volume → $250k – $500k |

**Total Year 2 revenue potential:** $2.5M – $7.5M (conservative to moderate).

### 2.7 Go-to-Market Summary (Two-Layer, Broker-First)

Most GTM strategies would start with licensed BDCs. Cuboid starts with brokers.

**Phase 0 (Months 0–3) – Stealth Broker Outreach (No Public Launch)**

- Identify 20–30 high-volume informal brokers in Lagos (bank worker networks).  
- Offer them early access to a "productivity tool" (no mention of compliance or licensing).  
- Focus on chat-to-trade, quote generation, and customer management.  
- Collect feedback and usage data. Do not charge fees yet.

**Phase 1 (Months 3–6) – Soft Launch with Licensed BDCs**

- Onboard 5–10 licensed BDCs who are willing to receive FX requests from brokers.  
- Brokers on the platform can see these BDCs' available inventory (anonymized or with markup).  
- Trades between brokers and BDCs are recorded. Cuboid takes a small fee.  
- Brokers still operate informally, but now with better tools. BDCs gain access to broker-driven volume.

**Phase 2 (Months 6–12) – Compliance Ladder Introduction**

- Begin nudging high-volume brokers: "You've completed 500 trades. Here's how to partner with a BDC or get licensed."  
- Introduce optional compliance features (identity verification, transaction limits) for brokers who want them.  
- Publicly position Cuboid as a BDC platform. Brokers remain a behind-the-scenes driver.

**Phase 3 (Months 12–18) – Regulator Engagement**

- Approach CBN and NFIU with data: "We have visibility into $X million in previously invisible FX flows. Here's a dashboard."  
- Demonstrate how brokers are being converted to licensed partners.  
- Formalize Cuboid as a recognized compliance utility.

### 2.8 Compliance Edge (Defensible, Not Naïve)

Cuboid's compliance approach acknowledges grey-market realities without crossing lines.

**What Cuboid does NOT do:**

- Explicitly market to unlicensed brokers as a "compliance-free FX tool."  
- Hide broker activity from regulators (audit trails exist and can be shared).  
- Facilitate settlement in ways that bypass banking controls.

**What Cuboid DOES do:**

- Builds a product that is *useful* to brokers (so they adopt it voluntarily).  
- Collects data on all activity (even from unlicensed users).  
- Maintains clear terms of service prohibiting unlicensed trading.  
- Provides a compliance ladder: informal → partnered with BDC → fully licensed.  
- Offers regulators a dashboard to see aggregated, anonymized flows.

**The legal theory:** Cuboid is a technology platform. It does not require users to be licensed to use basic features (customer management, quote generation). But any actual FX trade execution requires a licensed counterparty (a BDC) on at least one side. Brokers cannot trade anonymously with other brokers—they must route through a licensed BDC. This creates a compliance bridge rather than a loophole.

### 2.9 Funding Requirements (Revised – Minimum $5,500)

| Item | Amount (USD) | Notes |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Domain, hosting, Firebase/Supabase credits | $200 | AWS free tier for first year |
| UI/UX template (mobile-first, chat-style) | $300 | One-time purchase, customizable |
| Developer time (contract) – MVP | $3,000 | \~150 hours at $20/hr |
| Compliance consultation (broker-aware) | $500 | How to structure without legitimizing |
| Legal (terms of service, broker disclaimer) | $300 | Clear prohibition of unlicensed trading |
| Broker outreach & incentives (pilot) | $700 | WhatsApp campaigns, airtime, small referral bonuses |
| Contingency | $500 | Unexpected costs |
| **Total Minimum** | **$5,500** |  |

**This is an overly discounted strategic round.** Insane Technologies contributes pre-built modules (authentication, chat infrastructure, basic ledger) valued at $20,000+ at no cash cost, in exchange for their minimum 25% equity.

### 2.10 Equity Structure Disclosure

| Shareholder | Equity Stake | Contribution |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Insane Technologies | **Minimum 25%** | Technical infrastructure (chat, auth, ledger), strategic guidance, network access |
| Founding Team (operational) | 50% – 65% | Day-to-day execution, broker outreach, BDC onboarding, compliance setup |
| Strategic Investors ($5,500 round) | 5% – 15% (negotiable) | Cash, hands-on support, broker network access, regulatory introductions |

*Insane Technologies' 25% is a floor, not a ceiling. The $5,500 round dilutes only the founding team pool or is structured as a convertible note.*

### 2.11 Why $5,500 Is Realistic (Even with Broker Complexity)

Building a broker-aware platform for $5,500 sounds impossible. Here is why it is not:

1. **Existing infrastructure from Insane Technologies:** Chat, authentication, basic user management, and ledger logic already exist. Cuboid is not building from zero.  
     
2. **Lean MVP scope – broker features first:** The first version does not need automated CBN filing, complex regulator dashboards, or full inter-BDC matching. It needs chat-to-trade, quote generation, and basic customer management. That is 150 development hours.  
     
3. **Brokers are not expecting polish:** Brokers currently use WhatsApp. Any dedicated tool, even a basic one, is an upgrade. Perfection is not required.  
     
4. **Sweat equity:** The founding team and Insane Technologies take no cash salaries at this stage.  
     
5. **Revenue from month 2:** Brokers in the pilot will pay small transaction fees (or BDCs will pay subscriptions) to keep the platform running.

The $5,500 round is not meant to build the final product. It is meant to build a **live, usable MVP** that proves broker adoption, generates initial transaction volume, and attracts a larger $50k–$100k seed round at a much higher valuation.

### 2.12 The Ask to the Reader (Revised for Broker-Awareness)

This concept note is written for four audiences:

1. **Internal stakeholders and Insane Technologies:** To align on a broker-aware strategy that acknowledges market realities while maintaining regulatory defensibility.  
     
2. **Strategic partners (BDCs, fintechs, banks):** To understand that Cuboid's volume will come from both formal and informal channels, and that this is a feature, not a bug.  
     
3. **Hands-on investors in the $5,500 round:** To see how a tiny strategic investment, combined with Insane Technologies' 25%+ equity contribution, can capture value from a multi-billion-dollar grey market without crossing compliance lines.  
     
4. **Regulators (future engagement):** To demonstrate that Cuboid understands the real market, is building audit trails, and offers a pathway from invisibility to visibility.

After reviewing this document, the reader should understand:

- **Why informal brokers are the primary movers** and why ignoring them is a strategic error.  
- **How Cuboid appeals to brokers** without legitimizing unlicensed activity (two-layer design, compliance ladder, terms of service).  
- **Why $5,500 (plus Insane Technologies' contribution)** is sufficient to build a live, broker-adopted MVP.  
- **Why Insane Technologies holds at least 25% equity** as a strategic technical partner, not a passive investor.

## SECTION 3: VISION, MISSION & CORE VALUES (BROKER-INCLUSIVE)

### 3.1 Our Vision

To become the digital infrastructure that powers all retail FX movement in Nigeria—whether formal or informal, licensed or relationship-driven—by providing tools so useful that even the most efficient informal brokers choose to adopt them, while creating a transparent bridge to compliance for those who wish to formalize.

**Long-term statement (10 years):** A Nigerian FX market where every trusted broker has a digital tool that respects their workflow, every licensed BDC can compete fairly, and every regulator has visibility into flows without destroying the relationships and trust that make the market work.

**The nuance:** Cuboid does not dream of a world without informal brokers. That world is impossible. Instead, Cuboid dreams of a world where informal brokers operate with better tools, where they can voluntarily step into compliance when it benefits them, and where regulators can see enough to manage risk without crushing the agility that customers value.

### 3.2 Our Mission

To build and operate a lean, broker-aware digital FX platform that:

- **Respects the real workflow** of informal brokers (WhatsApp-speed, relationship-based, mobile-first) and gives them tools that feel familiar but more powerful.  
    
- **Serves licensed BDCs** with management modules, inter-BDC trading, and automated compliance—helping them compete with faster informal channels.  
    
- **Provides a compliance ladder** that allows any user—broker or BDC—to move from invisibility to full regulatory visibility at their own pace, with clear benefits at each step.  
    
- **Maintains regulatory defensibility** by holding audit trails, prohibiting unlicensed trading in terms of service, and ensuring every actual FX trade involves at least one licensed counterparty.  
    
- **Does all of the above with extreme capital efficiency** —proving that meaningful fintech infrastructure can be built for a minimum of $5,500 in strategic funding, with Insane Technologies contributing at least 25% equity as a long-term technical and strategic partner.

### 3.3 Core Values (Updated for Broker-Awareness)

#### 3.3.1 See the Market as It Is, Not as Regulators Wish It Were

Many fintechs design solutions based on how the market *should* work according to regulations. Cuboid designs based on how the market *actually* works. Informal brokers are primary movers. Bank workers source FX through relationships. WhatsApp is the trading floor. Any solution that pretends otherwise will be ignored.

**Operational expression:**

- The product team spends time in broker WhatsApp groups, observing workflows before writing code.  
- Features are tested with active brokers, not just licensed BDCs.  
- The roadmap prioritizes what brokers actually do (chat, quotes, phone calls) over what regulators wish they would do (reports, filings).

**But:** Seeing the market as it is does not mean endorsing illegality. Cuboid observes, learns, and builds tools that *can* be used compliantly—even if some users initially use them in grey areas.

#### 3.3.2 Compliance Is a Ladder, Not a Wall

Traditional compliance says: "You must be fully licensed to use any part of our platform." This creates a wall that keeps informal players out entirely. Cuboid replaces the wall with a ladder.

**The Cuboid Compliance Ladder:**

| Rung | User Status | Platform Access | Benefits | Regulatory Risk to Cuboid |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | Anonymous browser | View public rates, read documentation | None | None |
| 2 | Registered user (unverified) | Customer management, quote generation, chat | Productivity tools | Low (no trading) |
| 3 | Verified individual (ID uploaded) | Light escrow, trade requests to licensed BDCs | Faster matching | Moderate (trading facilitation) |
| 4 | Partnered with licensed BDC | Full trade execution via BDC umbrella | Compliance coverage, higher limits | Managed (BDC liable) |
| 5 | Licensed BDC or broker-licensee | Full platform: inter-trading, reporting, API | Complete access | Minimal (fully compliant) |

Users can climb the ladder at their own pace. Each rung offers clear benefits. Cuboid's terms of service make clear that trading without a license or BDC partner (Rung 4+) is prohibited.

**Operational expression:**

- Registration is free and requires only a phone number.  
- After 10 trade requests, the user sees: "You're moving significant volume. Here's how to partner with a BDC."  
- After 50 trade requests, the user sees compliance reminders and partnership offers.  
- The platform never blocks users for being unlicensed—but it persistently nudges them toward formalization.

#### 3.3.3 Build for Trust Networks, Not Anonymous Markets

The Nigerian FX market runs on trust. A customer deals with a broker because their cousin used that broker. A broker deals with a bank contact because they have settled successfully ten times before. Anonymous marketplaces (like a public FX exchange) fail because they lack this trust layer.

Cuboid builds trust networks into the product:

- **Reputation scores:** Visible to counterparties (e.g., "This broker has completed 500 trades with 98% on-time settlement").  
- **Mutual ratings:** After each trade, both parties rate each other.  
- **Network visualization:** A broker can see which of their trusted contacts are also on Cuboid.  
- **Escrow for new relationships:** First-time counterparties use light escrow; trusted pairs can settle directly.

**Operational expression:**

- No anonymous trading. Every user has an identity (verified at some level).  
- Trust scores are displayed prominently.  
- Users can block or report counterparties.  
- Cuboid does not match strangers automatically; it suggests matches based on network distance (friends of friends).

#### 3.3.4 Two-Layer GTM: Attract Brokers, Serve BDCs, Satisfy Regulators

Cuboid has three constituencies with different, sometimes conflicting, needs. The product and messaging must serve all three without alienating any.

| Constituency | What They Want | Cuboid's Message to Them |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Informal brokers | Speed, discretion, tools that work like WhatsApp | "We built the tool you wish you had. No compliance burden unless you want it." |
| Licensed BDCs | Volume, compliance tools, competitive edge | "We bring you broker-driven volume and digitize your operations." |
| Regulators | Visibility, compliance, data | "We have audit trails of previously invisible flows. Here is your dashboard." |

**Operational expression:**

- Different landing pages for different audiences.  
- Broker-facing communications never mention compliance or licensing.  
- BDC-facing communications emphasize compliance and volume.  
- Regulator-facing dashboards show aggregated, anonymized data by default, with drill-down to individual users available upon request and with proper authorization.

#### 3.3.5 Extreme Capital Efficiency (Unchanged from Previous)

A fintech does not need $1 million to prove product-market fit. Cuboid is being built with a minimum of $5,500 in strategic funding, leveraging existing infrastructure from Insane Technologies, sweat equity from the founding team, and lean third-party services.

**Operational expression:**

- No paid advertising until revenue is generated.  
- Open-source or low-cost tools preferred.  
- Feature prioritization is ruthless: if it does not directly enable a trade or a quote, it is deferred.

#### 3.3.6 Radical Transparency with Regulators (But Not at Broker Expense)

Cuboid will proactively offer regulators visibility into platform activity—but in a way that does not immediately expose individual brokers who are climbing the compliance ladder.

**The balance:**

- Regulators get aggregated dashboards (total volume, geographic distribution, suspicious activity patterns) by default.  
- Individual broker data is available but requires a formal request and proper legal basis.  
- Brokers are informed: "Your activity is recorded. Regulators can request this data. Here is how to formalize before that happens."

**Operational expression:**

- Audit trails are immutable and stored.  
- A regulator dashboard is built in Month 6, even if not yet shared.  
- Cuboid engages regulators proactively: "We have data on previously invisible flows. We want to share it with you in a responsible way. Help us design the compliance ladder."

#### 3.3.7 Insane Technologies as Strategic Anchor (Unchanged)

Insane Technologies holds a minimum of 25% equity in Cuboid, not as a passive investor but as an active technical and strategic contributor. This relationship provides Cuboid with access to pre-built modules (authentication, chat infrastructure, basic ledger) that would otherwise cost $20,000+ to develop.

**This is not a typical venture capital relationship.** It is a deep, long-term partnership where equity aligns incentives for both parties to succeed. Insane Technologies benefits only if Cuboid wins—and Cuboid wins only if brokers and BDCs adopt the platform.

### 3.4 Strategic Pillars (Broker-Aware)

| Pillar | Description | Key Metric |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **Broker Adoption** | Build tools so useful that informal brokers voluntarily switch from WhatsApp | 500 active brokers by Month 6 |
| **Compliance Ladder** | Convert broker volume into visible, formalized activity over time | 50 brokers moved to Rung 4+ (BDC-partnered) by Month 12 |
| **BDC Enablement** | Give licensed BDCs tools to compete with brokers and access broker-driven volume | 100 paying BDCs by Month 12 |
| **Regulator Partnership** | Provide dashboards and data that reduce regulatory blind spots | Formal no-objection letter by Month 9 |
| **Lean Execution** | Achieve all of the above with $5,500 strategic round | Positive unit economics by Month 8 |

### 3.5 What We Will Not Do (Updated for Broker-Awareness)

1. **Explicitly market to unlicensed brokers as a "trading platform."** Cuboid markets productivity tools (customer management, quote generation). Trading requires a licensed counterparty.  
     
2. **Hide broker activity from regulators.** Audit trails exist. Cuboid will share data when legally required.  
     
3. **Facilitate broker-to-broker anonymous trading.** Every trade must involve at least one licensed BDC on one side.  
     
4. **Pretend brokers do not exist.** That is the mistake most competitors make. Cuboid acknowledges reality and builds for it.  
     
5. **Rely on enforcement to drive compliance.** The compliance ladder uses incentives (better rates, higher limits, lower fees) not threats.

### 3.6 How Success Looks (Year 1 – Broker-Aware Milestones)

| Month | Milestone | Evidence |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Month 1 | $5,500 raised, legal entity formed, equity allocated (Insane Technologies 25%+) | Signed agreements |
| Month 2 | MVP live: chat-to-quote, customer management, basic registration | 20 broker signups (pilot) |
| Month 3 | First trade facilitated between a broker and a licensed BDC | $5,000 volume |
| Month 4 | 50 active brokers, 3 BDCs on platform | $50,000 monthly volume |
| Month 5 | Compliance ladder launched (nudges, partnership offers) | 5 brokers partner with BDCs |
| Month 6 | Regulator dashboard prototype; sandbox application submitted | Acknowledgment letter |
| Month 7 | 150 active brokers, 10 BDCs | $500,000 monthly volume |
| Month 8 | First revenue positive month (transaction fees \+ subscriptions) | $2,000+ MRR |
| Month 9 | Formal no-objection letter or sandbox approval | Regulatory green light |
| Month 10 | 300 brokers, 25 BDCs | $2M monthly volume |
| Month 11 | Compliance ladder success: 25 brokers formalized | Reduced regulatory risk |
| Month 12 | 500 brokers, 50 BDCs, $5M+ monthly volume | Seed round of $50k–$100k |

### 3.7 The Insane Technologies Commitment (Recap)

Because Insane Technologies holds a minimum 25% equity, Cuboid benefits from:

- **Technical baseline:** Access to existing code for authentication, chat, role-based access, basic transaction logging. Replacement cost: $20,000–$50,000.  
- **Strategic guidance:** Monthly advisory on product roadmap, broker strategy, regulatory engagement.  
- **Network access:** Introductions to broker networks, BDC associations, and regulatory contacts.  
- **Long-term alignment:** Insane Technologies will not dilute below 20% without founding team consent.

---

## SECTION 4: GLOSSARY OF TERMS (EXPANDED FOR BROKERS)

### 4.1 Core FX & Market Terms

| Term | Definition |
| :---- | :---- |
| **FX (Foreign Exchange)** | The market where one currency is traded for another. In Nigeria, the most common pair is USD/NGN. |
| **Retail FX** | Foreign exchange transactions for small to medium amounts (typically $500–$10,000) for personal or small business use. |
| **Parallel Market** | The unofficial FX market where rates may differ from the official CBN rate. Also called the "black market," though most participants do not consider it criminal. |
| **Spread** | The difference between the price at which a broker or BDC buys FX and the price at which they sell it. The spread is their profit. |

### 4.2 Broker-Specific Terms (New)

| Term | Definition |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Informal FX Broker** | An individual (often a bank worker, former bank worker, or trusted agent) who sources foreign currency through personal relationships and sells it to customers. Typically unlicensed. |
| **Bank Worker Broker** | A current employee of a commercial bank (teller, branch manager, treasury officer) who uses their internal access to source FX. This is usually against bank policy and may be illegal. |
| **Grey Market** | The space between formal (licensed BDCs) and illegal (criminal money laundering). Most informal brokers operate in the grey market—not fully illegal but not fully compliant. |
| **Trust Network** | The set of relationships a broker relies on to source FX. Trades happen because parties know and trust each other, not because of formal contracts. |
| **Chat-to-Trade** | A workflow where a user types a request in natural language (e.g., "need $5k USD for school fees") and the platform matches them with available inventory or suggests a quote. |
| **Quote Generation** | A feature that allows a broker to quickly produce a professional-looking rate quote (with expiry time, terms, and broker branding) to send to a customer via WhatsApp. |
| **Settlement Escrow (Light)** | A mechanism where customer funds are held temporarily while the broker sources FX. Funds are released to the broker only after delivery is confirmed. Reduces settlement risk. |
| **Compliance Ladder** | A structured pathway from anonymous/unverified user to fully licensed operator, with clear benefits at each rung. Designed to convert informal brokers gradually. |

### 4.3 Regulatory & Compliance Terms (Expanded)

| Term | Definition |
| :---- | :---- |
| **CBN (Central Bank of Nigeria)** | The apex bank responsible for currency policy, licensing BDCs, and enforcing FX regulations. |
| **NFIU (Nigerian Financial Intelligence Unit)** | The agency responsible for receiving and analyzing suspicious transaction reports (STRs) and currency transaction reports (CTRs). |
| **BDC (Bureau de Change)** | A licensed entity authorized to buy and sell foreign currency at retail levels. The formal channel for retail FX. |
| **Licensed BDC** | A BDC that has paid its license fees, filed its returns, and is recognized by the CBN. Approximately 5,000–5,800 exist in Nigeria. |
| **Unlicensed FX Trading** | Buying or selling foreign currency without a BDC license. This is technically illegal in Nigeria, though enforcement focuses on large-scale or criminal operations. |
| **Formalization** | The process by which an informal broker becomes a licensed BDC or partners formally with an existing BDC. |
| **No-Objection Letter** | A formal communication from a regulator stating they do not object to a proposed business activity. Not a license, but a critical signal of regulatory acceptance. |
| **Sandbox (Regulatory)** | A controlled environment where innovative financial products can be tested with real customers under relaxed rules. |
| **goAML** | The NFIU's software system for submitting STRs and CTRs. |

### 4.4 Platform & Technology Terms (Broker-Aware)

| Term | Definition |
| :---- | :---- |
| **MVP (Minimum Viable Product)** | The simplest version of Cuboid that still delivers value: chat-to-quote, customer management, basic registration, and trade logging with at least one licensed BDC on each trade. |
| **Broker Mode** | A user interface and feature set optimized for informal brokers: WhatsApp-style chat, quick quotes, customer lists, minimal compliance friction. |
| **BDC Mode** | A user interface and feature set for licensed BDCs: inventory management, compliance reporting, inter-BDC trading, regulator dashboards. |
| **Dual Interface** | The same platform presents different features and messaging depending on the user's declared status (broker vs BDC) and verification level. |
| **Trust Score** | A visible rating (0–100) assigned to each user based on trade completion rate, settlement speed, and counterparty ratings. |
| **Network Distance** | A measure of how many connections separate two users. Cuboid prioritizes matches between users who are "friends of friends" over strangers. |
| **Audit Trail** | An immutable log of every action: signup, quote, trade request, settlement, login. Stored and available for regulator review. |

### 4.5 Business & Partnership Terms (Updated)

| Term | Definition |
| :---- | :---- |
| **GTM (Go-to-Market)** | Cuboid's two-layer strategy: attract brokers through stealth outreach, onboard BDCs publicly, and demonstrate value to regulators. |
| **Strategic Round** | The $5,500 minimum funding round. Highly discounted. Open only to hands-on partners who bring network access, development capacity, or regulatory relationships. |
| **Insane Technologies** | The strategic equity holder holding a minimum of 25% of Cuboid. Provides technical infrastructure, strategic guidance, and network access at no cash cost. |
| **Broker Referral Program** | Brokers earn 10% of subscription fees for any BDC they refer to Cuboid for 12 months. Converts brokers into a sales channel. |
| **BDC Management Module** | A sellable add-on for licensed BDCs: inventory management, customer records, receipts, inter-BDC trading, compliance filing. |
| **MRR (Monthly Recurring Revenue)** | Predictable subscription revenue from BDCs using the BDC Management Module or compliance service. |

### 4.6 Risk & Legal Terms (Broker-Specific)

| Term | Definition |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Legitimization Risk** | The danger that Cuboid could be seen as endorsing or facilitating unlicensed FX trading. Mitigated by terms of service, audit trails, and requiring a licensed BDC on every trade. |
| **Plausible Deniability** | Cuboid's ability to honestly state to regulators: "We prohibit unlicensed trading in our terms. We do not market to unlicensed brokers. Our product is designed for licensed BDCs." Meanwhile, the product design appeals to brokers—but that is not illegal. |
| **Compliance Ladder** | The structured pathway from unverified user to fully licensed operator. A risk mitigation tool that converts grey-market volume into visible, compliant activity over time. |
| **Whistleblower Risk** | The danger that a disgruntled broker or competitor reports Cuboid to regulators for facilitating unlicensed activity. Mitigated by proactive regulator engagement and transparency. |

### 4.7 Acronyms Quick Reference (Expanded)

| Acronym | Full Meaning |
| :---- | :---- |
| BDC | Bureau de Change |
| CBN | Central Bank of Nigeria |
| NFIU | Nigerian Financial Intelligence Unit |
| FX | Foreign Exchange |
| USD | United States Dollar |
| NGN | Nigerian Naira |
| STR | Suspicious Transaction Report |
| CTR | Currency Transaction Report |
| AML | Anti-Money Laundering |
| KYC | Know Your Customer |
| KYB | Know Your Business |
| MVP | Minimum Viable Product |
| GTM | Go-to-Market |
| MRR | Monthly Recurring Revenue |
| API | Application Programming Interface |

### 4.8 Example Usage in a Sentence (Broker-Aware)

- **Informal FX Broker:** "The informal FX broker had 500 customers in his phone contacts but no way to track their requests until he started using Cuboid's customer management feature."  
    
- **Chat-to-Trade:** "Instead of calling ten people, the broker typed 'need $3k USD for medicals' into Cuboid's chat-to-trade and was matched with a BDC within two minutes."  
    
- **Compliance Ladder:** "After completing 200 trades, the broker received an offer to partner with a licensed BDC on Cuboid—moving from Rung 3 to Rung 4 of the compliance ladder."  
    
- **Legitimization Risk:** "Cuboid mitigates legitimization risk by requiring every trade to involve a licensed BDC on at least one side and by including clear prohibitions in its terms of service."  
    
- **Insane Technologies minimum 25% equity:** "Because Insane Technologies holds at least 25% equity, Cuboid launched with a pre-built chat infrastructure that would have cost $15,000 to develop from scratch."  
    
- **Strategic Round ($5,500):** "The $5,500 strategic round is not a valuation of Cuboid—it is an overly discounted entry for hands-on partners who believe in the broker-aware strategy."

## SECTION 5: THE REAL PRIMARY MOVERS – INFORMAL FX BROKERS & THEIR ECOSYSTEM

### 5.1 A Necessary Acknowledgment

Most formal analyses of the Nigerian FX market begin and end with licensed BDCs. They describe a tidy system where the CBN allocates dollars to banks, banks sell to BDCs, and BDCs sell to citizens. This description is not false, but it is dangerously incomplete.

**The complete picture:** The majority of retail FX transactions in Nigeria—by volume, by speed, and by customer preference—do not flow through licensed BDCs. They flow through **informal FX brokers**: individuals who have built trusted networks over years, who can source dollars faster than any licensed entity, and whose customers do not ask for receipts or regulatory approvals. They ask for dollars, and the broker delivers.

This section describes who these brokers are, how they work, why customers trust them, and why Cuboid must build with them in mind—without crossing regulatory lines.

### 5.2 Who Are the Informal FX Brokers?

Informal FX brokers are not a monolith. They come from different backgrounds, operate at different scales, and have different motivations. Understanding these segments is essential to designing a platform that appeals to them.

#### 5.2.1 Bank Worker Brokers (The Most Influential Segment)

**Who they are:** Current employees of commercial banks—tellers, branch managers, treasury officers, customer service representatives, and even some mid-level managers.

**How they access FX:** Their daily work gives them privileged information and access:

- Tellers see which accounts have dollar balances.  
- Branch managers know when the branch has excess USD inventory.  
- Treasury officers know interbank rates and can access wholesale windows.  
- Customer service representatives know which customers frequently send or receive dollars.

**How they operate:**  
A bank worker identifies a customer with dollar needs. They offer to "help" source USD at a better rate than the bank officially offers. The customer sends naira to the bank worker's personal account. The bank worker uses their internal access to obtain dollars (sometimes legitimately, sometimes through policy violations). The dollars are delivered via transfer or cash. The bank worker takes a spread of 2–5%. The bank never knows.

**Why they are important:**

- They have the most reliable access to FX within the banking system.  
- Their customers are often high-volume (business owners, frequent travelers).  
- They are highly motivated to keep their activities discreet.  
- They represent the greatest regulatory risk to Cuboid (bank employees violating policies).

**Estimated population:** 5,000–10,000 active bank worker brokers across Nigeria.

#### 5.2.2 Former Bank Worker Brokers

**Who they are:** Individuals who previously worked in banks, left (voluntarily or otherwise), but maintained their relationships with former colleagues still inside the banking system.

**How they access FX:** Their former colleagues give them preferential access, tip them off about available dollars, or process trades on their behalf.

**How they operate:**  
Similar to active bank workers, but with an additional layer of indirection. The former broker receives a customer request, contacts their former colleague at the bank, arranges the FX, and delivers to the customer. The former colleague takes a cut; the former broker takes a cut.

**Why they are important:**

- They are often more entrepreneurial than active bank workers (this is their primary income).  
- They are more likely to adopt digital tools because they are not constrained by bank policies.  
- They can scale beyond a single bank branch.

**Estimated population:** 3,000–6,000.

#### 5.2.3 Independent Trusted Agents

**Who they are:** Individuals with no formal banking background but with deep local trust. They may be small business owners, community leaders, or simply people known for "helping with dollars."

**How they access FX:** They aggregate demand from multiple customers, then source from bank worker brokers, licensed BDCs, or other independent agents. They are the last mile of the FX distribution chain.

**How they operate:**  
A customer in a small town needs $1,000. There is no BDC nearby. They call the local trusted agent. The agent collects the naira, finds a source in the nearest city (often a bank worker broker or BDC), arranges the trade, and delivers the dollars—sometimes physically traveling to collect cash.

**Why they are important:**

- They serve customers that licensed BDCs cannot reach profitably.  
- They are highly trusted at the local level.  
- They have the lowest individual volume but the highest customer count.

**Estimated population:** 10,000–20,000.

#### 5.2.4 Corporate Treasury Brokers

**Who they are:** Individuals working in the treasury departments of large corporations that receive dollar revenues (exporters, oil and gas companies, multinationals).

**How they access FX:** Their employer receives dollars legitimately. They divert a portion (sometimes with employer knowledge, sometimes without) to the parallel market, earning a spread.

**How they operate:**  
A company receives $1 million in export proceeds. The treasury officer reports $900,000 to the company and diverts $100,000 to broker networks. The dollars are sold at parallel market rates. The officer pockets the difference.

**Why they are important:**

- They control large volumes (tens of thousands of dollars per transaction).  
- They are the source of much of the liquidity in the parallel market.  
- They are the highest risk segment for Cuboid to engage with directly.

**Estimated population:** 500–1,000 (but each moves significant volume).

### 5.3 How Brokers Work: The Current Workflow

Despite their diversity, most informal brokers follow a similar workflow. Understanding this workflow is the key to building tools they will adopt.

| Step | Action | Current Tool | Pain Point |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | Customer reaches out with FX need | WhatsApp, phone call, text message | No structured request; details often missed |
| 2 | Broker checks inventory across sources | Phone calls to 5–20 contacts | Slow, exhausting, no visibility into who has dollars |
| 3 | Broker quotes a rate | Mental math or quick calculator | Rate varies by customer; inconsistent |
| 4 | Customer agrees | Verbal confirmation by call or text | No binding commitment; customers sometimes back out |
| 5 | Broker confirms with source | Second round of calls | Double work; source may have sold to someone else |
| 6 | Customer sends naira | Bank transfer (personal account) or cash | Settlement risk: customer pays, broker may fail to deliver |
| 7 | Broker sends dollars or arranges delivery | Bank transfer, cash handover, or physical courier | Settlement risk: source may fail broker |
| 8 | Broker records the trade | WhatsApp message, notebook, or nothing | No history; cannot serve repeat customers efficiently |

**The total time from customer request to settlement:** 30 minutes to 4 hours, depending on network responsiveness.

**The broker's margin:** Typically 1–5% of transaction value. A broker who moves $50,000 per week (common for active bank worker brokers) earns $500–$2,500 per week in spreads.

### 5.4 Why Customers Trust Brokers Over BDCs

This is a critical insight. Most formal analyses assume customers prefer licensed BDCs because they are "official" and "safe." In practice, customers prefer brokers because:

| Factor | Broker | Licensed BDC |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Speed | Minutes to hours | Hours to days (if inventory available) |
| Rate | Negotiable, often better | Fixed, often worse (BDCs have higher costs) |
| Trust | Personal relationship, proven track record | Anonymous counter; no relationship |
| Convenience | Comes to customer (WhatsApp, phone) | Customer must go to BDC shop |
| Receipt | Not needed or accepted | Receipt not valued by most customers |
| Recourse | Personal relationship provides leverage | Limited recourse; BDC may be unresponsive |

**The uncomfortable truth for regulators:** For most retail FX customers, the informal broker provides a better experience than the licensed BDC. Cuboid does not need to agree with this reality. But Cuboid must build for it.

### 5.5 Broker Pain Points (Why They Would Adopt a Digital Tool)

Despite their efficiency, brokers face significant pain points that a well-designed digital tool could solve.

#### 5.5.1 Inventory Visibility

**The pain:** A broker never knows who has dollars at any given moment. They must call or message multiple contacts, wait for replies, and hope the inventory is still available when they circle back.

**The cost:** Hours of daily phone time. Missed trades because a source sold to someone else while the broker was confirming with their customer.

**What Cuboid offers:** A real-time, opt-in inventory view where sources can indicate "I have $X available at Y rate." Brokers can see available inventory without calling.

**The broker's reaction (predicted):** "Finally. I have been asking for this for years."

#### 5.5.2 Settlement Risk

**The pain:** A broker commits to delivering dollars to a customer, but their source fails to deliver. The broker now faces an angry customer, potential reputational damage, and possible financial loss.

**The cost:** Lost customers, damaged reputation, occasional out-of-pocket losses.

**What Cuboid offers:** Light escrow. Customer funds are held temporarily. Dollars are confirmed before funds are released to the broker. If the source fails, funds return to customer.

**The broker's reaction (predicted):** "This protects me too. I don't have to chase sources for proof of delivery."

#### 5.5.3 Customer Management

**The pain:** A broker has hundreds of customers in their phone contacts. They cannot remember who asked for what, who is due for a follow-up, or who has paid late before.

**The cost:** Lost repeat business. Wasted time searching WhatsApp history.

**What Cuboid offers:** A simple customer database: names, contact info, past requests, payment history, trust score.

**The broker's reaction (predicted):** "I didn't know I needed this until I saw it."

#### 5.5.4 Scaling Beyond Personal Network

**The pain:** A broker's volume is limited by their personal network. They cannot easily find new sources or new customers.

**The cost:** Capped income. Competitors with larger networks win.

**What Cuboid offers:** Introductions to vetted sources (licensed BDCs and other brokers who have opted into discovery). Not anonymous matching, but "friends of friends" recommendations based on trust scores.

**The broker's reaction (predicted):** "This is dangerous for my business model if everyone can see everyone. But if I control who sees me, maybe useful."

#### 5.5.5 Regulatory Anxiety (The Silent Pain)

**The pain:** Most brokers know they are operating in a grey area. They worry about a whistleblower, a regulator crackdown, or a bank freezing their accounts.

**The cost:** Constant low-level anxiety. Inability to plan for the long term. Cash hoarding.

**What Cuboid offers:** A clear pathway to formalization. "You do not have to stop. But here is how to formalize so you never worry again."

**The broker's reaction (predicted):** "I will never fully formalize—too much cost, too much visibility. But I want to know my options."

### 5.6 The Broker's Relationship with Licensed BDCs

The relationship between brokers and BDCs is complex and varies by segment.

| Scenario | Relationship Type | Frequency |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Broker sources from BDC | Broker buys dollars from a BDC (often at wholesale rates) and resells to customers | Common |
| BDC sources from broker | BDC buys from broker when BDC inventory is low | Less common but happens |
| Broker and BDC are the same person | Individual holds a BDC license but also operates informally | Uncommon but exists |
| Broker and BDC compete | Both serve the same customers; customer chooses based on rate/speed | Very common |
| Broker refers to BDC | Broker sends customers to a BDC for a referral fee | Rare (brokers keep customers) |

**The insight:** Brokers and BDCs are not enemies. They are overlapping ecosystems. A platform that serves both can capture volume regardless of which entity executes the trade.

### 5.7 Why Brokers Have Not Already Formalized

If formalization (becoming a licensed BDC or partnering with one) offers safety and legitimacy, why do most brokers remain informal?

| Barrier | Explanation |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Cost** | A BDC license costs hundreds of thousands of naira, plus annual fees, plus compliance staff. |
| **Visibility** | Once licensed, transactions are reported to CBN. Brokers lose discretion. |
| **Bank account risk** | Licensed BDCs are scrutinized more heavily. Informal brokers use personal accounts. |
| **Speed** | Licensed BDCs must follow reporting rules, slowing down trade execution. |
| **No perceived benefit** | Customers do not demand a license. Why pay for something customers do not value? |

**The Cuboid approach:** Do not force formalization. Make it optional, beneficial, and gradual. The compliance ladder does not punish informal brokers—it rewards those who choose to climb.

### 5.8 The Volume Sizing Problem (Nobody Knows the Real Numbers)

Official statistics on broker-driven FX volume do not exist because brokers are invisible by design. Cuboid has developed estimates based on:

- Triangulation from CBN data on total FX流入 (inflow) minus formal BDC-reported sales.  
- Interviews with brokers who disclosed their weekly volumes (with anonymity).  
- Bank transaction data (anonymized, aggregated) showing patterns consistent with broker activity.

**Estimated annual retail FX volume by channel:**

| Channel | Annual Volume (USD) | Share | Visibility to Regulator |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Licensed BDCs (reported) | $5B – $8B | 20–30% | High (but often inaccurate) |
| Licensed BDCs (unreported) | $2B – $4B | 10–15% | Low |
| Informal brokers (bank worker) | $6B – $10B | 25–35% | None |
| Informal brokers (independent) | $3B – $5B | 10–20% | None |
| Corporate treasury diversion | $2B – $4B | 10–15% | None |
| **Total retail FX turnover** | **$18B – $31B** | **100%** |  |

**The implication:** Formal BDCs (reported) represent only 20–30% of actual retail FX volume. The remaining 70–80% is invisible to regulators. Cuboid's opportunity is not to replace the formal 20–30%. It is to bring visibility to the invisible 70–80%.

### 5.9 The Regulatory Risk of Acknowledging Brokers

CBN and NFIU may be uncomfortable with a platform that explicitly acknowledges informal brokers. Cuboid mitigates this through:

| Mitigation | Description |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Terms of service** | Explicitly prohibit unlicensed FX trading. Brokers who use Cuboid for trading violate terms. |
| **Licensed counterparty requirement** | Every trade on Cuboid must involve at least one licensed BDC on one side. No broker-to-broker anonymous trading. |
| **Audit trails** | All activity is logged and available to regulators upon request. |
| **Proactive engagement** | Cuboid approaches regulators with data: "We have visibility into previously invisible flows. Here is how we can help you." |
| **Compliance ladder** | Brokers are nudged toward formalization. The platform is a conversion tool, not an endorsement of informality. |

**The message to regulators:** "We see the same problem you see—80% of retail FX is invisible. We have built a platform that makes that invisibility visible, without destroying the trust and speed that customers value. Work with us."

### 5.10 Summary: Why Cuboid Builds for Brokers

| Reason | Explanation |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Volume** | Brokers control 70–80% of retail FX volume. Ignoring them means ignoring most of the market. |
| **Trust** | Customers trust brokers more than BDCs. Any platform that excludes brokers excludes customer trust. |
| **Speed** | Brokers are faster than BDCs. Cuboid must match their speed to be adopted. |
| **Conversion opportunity** | Brokers are not enemies of compliance. They are potential formalization candidates. |
| **Competitive moat** | Competitors that ignore brokers will build inferior platforms. Brokers will not use them. |

**The final point:** Cuboid is not a "broker platform." Cuboid is a platform that licensed BDCs use—and that brokers find so useful they use it anyway, knowing they are in a grey area, while Cuboid maintains regulatory defensibility through terms of service, licensed counterparty requirements, and audit trails.

---

## SECTION 6: LICENSED BDCs – FORMAL BUT FRAGMENTED

### 6.1 The Formal Channel's Role

While brokers dominate volume and speed, licensed BDCs remain the only legal channel for retail FX distribution. Every dollar that flows through a broker ultimately traces back to a bank, a corporate treasury, or—sometimes—a licensed BDC. BDCs are not irrelevant. They are simply outmatched.

**The BDC's competitive disadvantages against brokers:**

| Factor | Licensed BDC | Informal Broker | Advantage |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Speed | Hours to days | Minutes to hours | Broker |
| Compliance burden | High (CBN/NFIU reports) | None | Broker |
| Operating cost | Rent, staff, license fees | Minimal (phone, WhatsApp) | Broker |
| Customer relationship | Transactional (customer visits shop) | Relational (WhatsApp, phone) | Broker |
| Pricing flexibility | Constrained by CBN guidelines | Fully flexible | Broker |
| Inventory visibility | Only knows own inventory | Can see network of sources | Broker |

**The result:** Licensed BDCs are losing market share to brokers, especially in urban areas where broker networks are dense.

### 6.2 BDC Demographics and Distribution

As of 2024, Nigeria has approximately 5,000–5,800 licensed BDCs. However, "licensed" does not mean "active and compliant."

| Category | Estimated Count | Characteristics |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Active, compliant, digital-savvy | 500–800 | Large BDCs in major cities; use computers; file reports (mostly) |
| Active, semi-compliant, manual | 2,000–3,000 | Most BDCs; use Excel or paper; file reports late or inaccurately |
| Active, non-compliant | 500–1,000 | Trade but do not file; high regulatory risk |
| Dormant (license held but inactive) | 1,000–1,500 | License not revoked but no active trading |

**Geographic concentration:**

| City | Estimated BDCs | Share | Notes |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Lagos | 1,500 – 2,000 | 30–35% | Highest density; most competitive |
| Kano | 500 – 700 | 10–15% | Major northern hub |
| Abuja | 400 – 600 | 8–12% | Political capital; regulator presence |
| Port Harcourt | 300 – 500 | 6–10% | Oil and gas center |
| Ibadan | 200 – 300 | 4–6% | Large city but less FX intensity |
| Other cities | 1,500 – 2,000 | 30–35% | Distributed across Nigeria |

### 6.3 The BDC Business Model (Simplified)

A licensed BDC's revenue comes from the spread between their purchase price and sale price.

**Typical BDC economics (pre-2023, normalized):**

| Metric | Value |
| :---- | :---- |
| Average purchase price (from bank or source) | NGN 750 per USD |
| Average sale price (to customer) | NGN 770 per USD |
| Spread | NGN 20 per USD (2.7%) |
| Average daily volume | $10,000 – $50,000 |
| Daily gross profit (spread × volume) | $200 – $1,000 |
| Monthly operating costs (rent, staff, compliance) | $1,000 – $5,000 |
| Monthly net profit | $5,000 – $25,000 (for active BDCs) |

**Post-2023 (naira volatility):** Spreads have widened (5–10%), volumes have fluctuated, and many BDCs have become less profitable due to inventory mismatches and regulatory fines.

### 6.4 BDC Pain Points (Detailed)

#### 6.4.1 Inventory Mismatch (The Same Problem Brokers Have)

**The pain:** A BDC either has too many dollars (idle inventory, opportunity cost) or too few (turning away customers, losing revenue). Unlike brokers, BDCs cannot easily trade with other BDCs to balance inventory.

**The cost:** Idle inventory costs 5–10% annual opportunity cost. Shortages cost lost revenue (customers go to brokers or competitors).

**Current solution:** Calling other BDCs they know, asking for trades. Same as brokers. Same inefficiency.

**What Cuboid offers:** Inter-BDC trading module—a simple, fast way to see which BDCs have excess or deficit inventory and execute trades instantly.

#### 6.4.2 Compliance Burden (Unlike Brokers)

**The pain:** BDCs must file daily returns, weekly positions, and suspicious transaction reports with CBN and NFIU. This takes hours per week, requires dedicated staff, and carries fines for late or incorrect filings.

**The cost:** Compliance officer salary ($2,000–$5,000 per month for large BDCs). Fines ($500–$10,000 per infraction). Time spent on filing (10–20 hours per week for medium BDCs).

**Current solution:** Excel templates, manual data entry, and hope.

**What Cuboid offers:** Automated compliance filing. Trade data is captured once; reports are generated automatically and can be submitted with one click (or via API to CBN/NFIU in the future).

#### 6.4.3 Competition from Brokers (The Silent Existential Threat)

**The pain:** Brokers offer faster service, better rates (to customers), and no compliance overhead. Many BDCs are losing customers to brokers—including customers who used to come to the BDC shop.

**The cost:** Declining volume, declining revenue, declining relevance.

**Current solution:** Some BDCs have started using WhatsApp to mimic brokers. Others have lowered prices to compete. Neither works sustainably.

**What Cuboid offers:** Instead of competing with brokers, BDCs can source from brokers and serve brokers. Cuboid allows BDCs to:

- See broker demand and offer inventory to brokers.  
- Accept trade requests from brokers (new customer channel).  
- Use brokers as distribution partners (broker sells to end customer; BDC supplies FX).

**The strategic shift:** BDCs stop fighting brokers and start feeding them—while keeping the compliance layer that brokers lack.

#### 6.4.4 Lack of Digital Tools

**The pain:** Most BDCs use Excel or paper for inventory, customer records, and receipts. This is error-prone, time-consuming, and impossible to audit.

**The cost:** Errors in inventory lead to lost trades or over-selling (delivering dollars not actually held). Poor customer records mean lost repeat business.

**Current solution:** Expensive custom software ($5,000+ upfront) that BDCs cannot afford or maintain.

**What Cuboid offers:** The BDC Management Module—a monthly subscription ($20–$100) that provides inventory management, customer records, digital receipts, and compliance filing in one mobile-friendly dashboard.

#### 6.4.5 Regulatory Anxiety (Shared with Brokers)

**The pain:** BDCs fear CBN inspections, license revocation, and fines. Unlike brokers, BDCs cannot hide. They are visible targets.

**The cost:** Constant low-level anxiety. Conservative trading (turning away volume to avoid scrutiny).

**Current solution:** Hire compliance consultants. Keep paper records ready for inspection.

**What Cuboid offers:** An audit trail that is always ready. A regulator dashboard (with BDC permission) that shows real-time compliance. Proof of good behavior.

### 6.5 Why BDCs Would Adopt Cuboid

| Motivation | Explanation |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Volume from brokers** | Cuboid connects BDCs to broker demand—a new customer channel. |
| **Inter-BDC trading** | BDCs can balance inventory without phone calls and manual trades. |
| **Compliance automation** | Reduce filing time from hours to minutes. Avoid fines. |
| **Cost savings** | Replace expensive custom software with low-cost monthly subscription. |
| **Competitive parity** | Brokers use digital tools (WhatsApp). BDCs need their own digital tools to compete. |

### 6.6 The BDC's Relationship with Brokers (Revisited)

Cuboid does not force BDCs to love brokers. But it gives BDCs tools to profit from broker activity.

| BDC Strategy | Without Cuboid | With Cuboid |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Ignore brokers | Lose volume to brokers | Still lose volume |
| Fight brokers | Price war, lower margins | Price war, lower margins |
| Feed brokers (supply FX to brokers) | Manual, risky, no tracking | Automated, tracked, compliant |

**The Cuboid model:** BDCs become the compliant backbone for broker-driven volume. Brokers get better sourcing. BDCs get volume without having to chase retail customers directly. Regulators get visibility.

### 6.7 BDC Segmentation for GTM

Not all BDCs will adopt Cuboid at the same time. Cuboid will target segments in order.

| Priority | Segment | Characteristics | GTM Approach |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | Digital-savvy, compliance-conscious | Already using some digital tools; understand value of automation | Direct sales, product demo |
| 2 | High-volume, frustrated with manual | Losing volume to brokers; want to compete | ROI calculator, broker volume promise |
| 3 | Mid-volume, risk-averse | Fearful of regulation; want compliance help | Compliance-first messaging |
| 4 | Low-volume, low-engagement | May never adopt | Ignore until later phases |

**Target for Year 1:** 100 BDCs (Priority 1 and 2 segments).

### 6.8 The BDC Management Module (Preview)

The BDC Management Module is the primary sellable product for licensed BDCs. It will be detailed in Section 12, but a preview is useful here.

| Feature | Description | Value to BDC |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Inventory dashboard | Real-time view of USD/NGN/other holdings | Know position instantly |
| Customer management | Store customer KYC, request history, preferences | Serve repeat customers faster |
| Digital receipts | Generate CBN-compliant receipts with QR codes | Audit-ready; professional |
| Inter-BDC trading | See other BDCs' inventory; execute peer trades | Balance inventory, reduce idle USD |
| Compliance filing | Auto-generate CBN/NFIU reports | Save hours, avoid fines |
| Broker demand feed | See requests from brokers in your area | New revenue channel |
| Settlement tracking | Track incoming/outgoing payments | Reduce settlement risk |

**Pricing:** $20–$100 per month depending on volume and features. Lower than any comparable software.

### 6.9 Summary: BDCs \+ Brokers on One Platform

| Without Cuboid | With Cuboid |
| :---- | :---- |
| BDCs compete with brokers (losing) | BDCs supply to brokers (winning) |
| BDCs have manual operations | BDCs have digital operations |
| BDCs file compliance manually (late, error-prone) | BDCs file compliance automatically |
| BDCs cannot trade with each other | BDCs trade inter-BDC instantly |
| BDCs have no visibility into broker demand | BDCs see broker demand and respond |

**The Cuboid advantage:** Instead of choosing between brokers and BDCs, Cuboid serves both. Brokers get speed and tools. BDCs get volume and compliance. Regulators get visibility. This is not a zero-sum game. It is a platform that makes the entire ecosystem more efficient.

**End of Section 5 and Section 6**

I have now completed **Section 5 (The Real Primary Movers – Informal FX Brokers & Their Ecosystem)** and **Section 6 (Licensed BDCs – Formal But Fragmented)**.

Shall I proceed with **Section 7 (Stakeholder Pain Points Analysis – Including Brokers as a Category)** and **Section 8 (Market Opportunity & Sizing – Formal \+ Grey Market)** next?

Here are **Section 7** and **Section 8** of the Cuboid Business Concept Note, fully rewritten with the broker-aware context. Formatted for Google Docs copy-paste.
