## SECTION 7: STAKEHOLDER PAIN POINTS ANALYSIS (INCLUDING BROKERS AS A CATEGORY)

### 7.1 Introduction to Stakeholder Mapping (Revised)

The Cuboid ecosystem includes six primary stakeholder groups. Unlike most concept notes, this analysis places **informal brokers** at the center—not because Cuboid endorses unlicensed activity, but because brokers are the primary movers of retail FX volume. Understanding their pain points is essential to building a platform they will adopt.

**The six stakeholder groups:**

| Group | Role in Ecosystem | Decision Power | Regulatory Status |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Informal FX Brokers | Source and distribute FX via trust networks | High (control volume) | Unlicensed (grey market) |
| Licensed BDCs | Legal retail FX distribution | Medium (declining) | Licensed, regulated |
| Regulators (CBN, NFIU) | Set rules, enforce compliance, monitor flows | Absolute (can shut down) | Government |
| Commercial Banks | Provide settlement, hold accounts, source of FX | High (gatekeepers) | Licensed, regulated |
| Fintechs & PSPs | Want to offer FX but need BDC/broker partners | Low (dependent) | Varies |
| End Customers | Need FX for school fees, travel, medical, business | Low (individual) | None |

### 7.2 Informal FX Brokers – Pain Points (Detailed)

This is the most important section for product design. Brokers will only adopt Cuboid if it solves real pains they experience daily.

#### 7.2.1 Inventory Discovery Pain

**The problem:** A broker never knows who has FX available at any given moment. They must call or message 5–20 contacts sequentially, waiting for replies. By the time they find a source, the inventory may be gone or the rate may have changed.

**Current coping mechanism:** Maintaining a "favorites" list of reliable sources. Calling them in order of trust. Accepting that some trades will fail.

**Cost of this pain:**

- **Time:** 2–4 hours daily on phone calls and WhatsApp messages.  
- **Missed trades:** 10–30% of customer requests cannot be fulfilled because no source found in time.  
- **Frustration:** Brokers describe this as their \#1 daily annoyance.

**Cuboid solution:** Real-time, opt-in inventory visibility. Sources (BDCs or other brokers) mark available inventory and rates. Brokers see available inventory instantly without calling.

**Metric of success:** Reduce broker phone time by 50% within 30 days of adopting Cuboid.

#### 7.2.2 Settlement Risk Pain

**The problem:** A broker commits to delivering dollars to a customer, but their source fails to deliver (sold to someone else, rate changed, bank transfer delayed). The broker now faces an angry customer, reputational damage, and potential financial loss if they must compensate the customer.

**Current coping mechanism:** Only trade with trusted sources who have a history of reliable delivery. Avoid new sources. Accept occasional failures as cost of business.

**Cost of this pain:**

- **Lost customers:** Each failed delivery risks losing a customer permanently.  
- **Reputational damage:** Brokers rely on word-of-mouth. Failures spread quickly.  
- **Out-of-pocket losses:** Some brokers refund customers out of pocket to preserve reputation.

**Cuboid solution:** Light escrow. Customer funds are held temporarily. Dollars are confirmed (via source confirmation or settlement proof) before funds are released to the broker. If source fails, funds return to customer.

**Metric of success:** Reduce trade failure rate from 10% to \<2% for Cuboid-facilitated trades.

#### 7.2.3 Customer Management Pain

**The problem:** A broker has hundreds of customer contacts stored in their phone—names, phone numbers, occasional notes. There is no way to track who asked for what, who is due for follow-up, who has paid late before, or who is a high-value repeat customer.

**Current coping mechanism:** Scrolling through WhatsApp history. Relying on memory. Losing track of customers who do not follow up.

**Cost of this pain:**

- **Lost repeat business:** 20–40% of customers are not followed up because broker forgets.  
- **Wasted time:** 1–2 hours daily searching for past conversations.  
- **Poor customer experience:** "Didn't I already tell you my rate?" leads to customer frustration.

**Cuboid solution:** Simple customer database within the platform. Each customer record includes name, contact info, past requests, payment history, and broker notes. Optional reminders for follow-up.

**Metric of success:** 80% of active brokers use customer management feature within 60 days.

#### 7.2.4 Scaling Beyond Personal Network Pain

**The problem:** A broker's volume is limited by the size of their personal network. They cannot easily find new sources (who have available FX) or new customers (who need FX). Growth requires years of relationship building.

**Current coping mechanism:** Accept capped volume. Occasionally get introduced to new contacts through existing relationships.

**Cost of this pain:**

- **Capped income:** Broker cannot grow beyond what their current network supports.  
- **Competitor advantage:** Brokers with larger networks win more trades.

**Cuboid solution:** "Friends of friends" discovery. Brokers can opt into limited visibility, showing their available inventory (or demand) to brokers who are within 2–3 network hops. Not anonymous—they see who they are dealing with—but expanded reach beyond direct contacts.

**Metric of success:** 30% of brokers report new trading relationships formed through Cuboid within 90 days.

#### 7.2.5 Regulatory Anxiety Pain (Silent)

**The problem:** Most brokers know they are operating in a grey area. They worry about whistleblowers, regulator crackdowns, bank account freezes, or legal consequences. This anxiety affects their behavior—they hoard cash, avoid electronic trails, and cannot plan for the long term.

**Current coping mechanism:** Denial. "Everyone does it." "They won't catch me." Cash preference.

**Cost of this pain:**

- **Cash hoarding:** Increased risk of theft or loss.  
- **Inability to scale:** Cannot accept electronic payments or build a formal business.  
- **Constant anxiety:** Brokers describe this as a background stress that never goes away.

**Cuboid solution:** A clear, opt-in compliance ladder. "You do not have to formalize today. But here is how to formalize when you are ready. And here are the benefits (better rates, higher limits, lower anxiety)."

**Metric of success:** 10% of active brokers begin formalization process (partner with a BDC or inquire about licensing) within 12 months.

#### 7.2.6 Broker Pain Points Summary Table

| Pain Point | Severity (1-10) | Cuboid Solution | Expected Adoption Driver |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Inventory discovery | 9 | Real-time inventory visibility | Primary reason to use Cuboid |
| Settlement risk | 8 | Light escrow | Secondary reason |
| Customer management | 6 | Customer database | "Nice to have" but valuable |
| Scaling network | 7 | Friends-of-friends discovery | Growth-oriented brokers |
| Regulatory anxiety | 5 | Compliance ladder | Long-term retention |

### 7.3 Licensed BDCs – Pain Points (Detailed)

While brokers are primary movers, BDCs remain the only legal channel. Their pain points differ significantly.

#### 7.3.1 Inventory Mismatch Pain (Inter-BDC Trading Gap)

**The problem:** A BDC has excess USD in Lagos but cannot easily sell to a BDC with shortage in Abuja. Current solution is phone calls, manual negotiation, and bank transfers—same as brokers.

**Current coping mechanism:** Maintain relationships with 5–10 other BDCs. Call them when inventory is imbalanced.

**Cost of this pain:**

- **Idle inventory:** Holding USD with no customer demand costs 5–10% annual opportunity cost.  
- **Lost sales:** Turning away customers when inventory is low.  
- **Inefficient pricing:** Cannot see market-wide rates; may sell too low or buy too high.

**Cuboid solution:** Inter-BDC trading module. BDCs can see excess/deficit inventory from other BDCs and execute trades instantly with automated settlement.

**Metric of success:** 50% of BDC-to-BDC trades previously done by phone move to Cuboid within 6 months.

#### 7.3.2 Compliance Burden Pain

**The problem:** BDCs must file daily returns, weekly positions, and suspicious transaction reports with CBN and NFIU. Filing is manual, time-consuming, and error-prone. Fines for late or incorrect filings are common.

**Current coping mechanism:** Hire a compliance officer (large BDCs) or dedicate a staff member to filing (small BDCs). Use Excel templates provided by CBN.

**Cost of this pain:**

- **Labor cost:** $2,000–$5,000 per month for compliance staff.  
- **Fines:** $500–$10,000 per infraction. Many BDCs pay fines annually.  
- **Time:** 10–20 hours per week on filing for medium BDCs.

**Cuboid solution:** Automated compliance filing. Trade data captured once. Reports generated automatically. One-click submission (or API to CBN/NFIU in future).

**Metric of success:** Reduce BDC compliance filing time by 80% within 90 days of adoption.

#### 7.3.3 Competition from Brokers Pain

**The problem:** Brokers offer faster service, better rates (to customers), and no compliance overhead. BDCs are losing market share, especially for smaller retail transactions.

**Current coping mechanism:** Some BDCs have started using WhatsApp to mimic brokers. Others have lowered prices, squeezing margins. Neither solves the structural disadvantage.

**Cost of this pain:**

- **Declining volume:** 10–30% year-over-year loss for some BDCs.  
- **Margin compression:** Lower prices reduce profitability.  
- **Relevance:** BDCs risk becoming irrelevant for retail FX.

**Cuboid solution:** Instead of fighting brokers, BDCs can supply to brokers. Cuboid shows BDCs broker demand in their area. BDCs become the compliant backbone for broker-driven volume.

**Metric of success:** BDCs using Cuboid report increased volume from broker channel within 60 days.

#### 7.3.4 Lack of Digital Tools Pain

**The problem:** Most BDCs use Excel or paper for inventory, customer records, and receipts. This is error-prone, time-consuming, and impossible to audit.

**Current coping mechanism:** Expensive custom software ($5,000+ upfront) that most BDCs cannot afford. Or continue with Excel.

**Cost of this pain:**

- **Errors:** Inventory mistakes lead to over-selling or missed trades.  
- **Labor:** Manual data entry takes hours daily.  
- **Audit risk:** Regulator finds incomplete records; fines or suspension.

**Cuboid solution:** BDC Management Module – low-cost monthly subscription ($20–$100) with inventory, customer management, digital receipts, and compliance filing.

**Metric of success:** 100 BDCs paying for BDC Management Module within 12 months.

#### 7.3.5 BDC Pain Points Summary Table

| Pain Point | Severity (1-10) | Cuboid Solution | Expected Adoption Driver |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Inventory mismatch | 8 | Inter-BDC trading | Immediate ROI |
| Compliance burden | 9 | Automated filing | Primary sales hook |
| Competition from brokers | 7 | Broker demand feed | Strategic necessity |
| Lack of digital tools | 6 | BDC Management Module | Operational efficiency |

### 7.4 Regulators (CBN, NFIU) – Pain Points

Regulators are often seen as adversaries, but they have genuine pain points that Cuboid can help solve.

#### 7.4.1 No Visibility into Real Market

**The problem:** Regulators have no real-time visibility into FX flows. They receive reports days or weeks late, and only from licensed entities. The majority of volume (broker-driven) is invisible.

**Current coping mechanism:** Physical inspections, enforcement actions, relying on banks for data.

**Cost of this pain:**

- **Ineffective policy:** Cannot make informed decisions without real data.  
- **High supervision cost:** Physical inspections require travel and staff time.  
- **Enforcement lag:** Problems are detected weeks or months after they occur.

**Cuboid solution:** Regulator dashboard showing aggregated, anonymized FX flows from platform activity. Drill-down available upon request.

**Metric of success:** CBN or NFIU requests formal dashboard access within 12 months.

#### 7.4.2 Manual Data Aggregation

**The problem:** BDCs submit reports as Excel files via email. Regulators must manually compile, clean, and analyze this data.

**Current coping mechanism:** Dedicated data entry team. Manual validation.

**Cost of this pain:**

- **Labor cost:** $500,000–$1,000,000 annually for data processing staff.  
- **Data errors:** Manual entry introduces errors.  
- **Delayed analysis:** Reports are weeks old before analysis begins.

**Cuboid solution:** API-based automated reporting. Cuboid can push structured data directly to regulator systems (goAML, etc.) with proper integration.

**Metric of success:** Pilot integration with NFIU goAML within 18 months.

#### 7.4.3 Inconsistent Data Quality

**The problem:** Even when BDCs file reports, the data is often wrong—inventories don't match, trades are omitted, numbers are guessed.

**Current coping mechanism:** Follow-up calls, audits, fines.

**Cost of this pain:**

- **Distrust of data:** Regulators cannot rely on reported numbers.  
- **Enforcement burden:** Chasing inaccurate reports consumes resources.

**Cuboid solution:** Data is captured at trade execution, not entered manually later. Inventory is tracked in real time. Reports are generated from live data, not memory.

**Metric of success:** 100% accuracy on compliance reports generated by Cuboid (no manual errors).

#### 7.4.4 Regulator Pain Points Summary Table

| Pain Point | Severity (1-10) | Cuboid Solution | Regulatory Appeal |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| No real-time visibility | 10 | Regulator dashboard | Very high |
| Manual data aggregation | 8 | API-based reporting | High |
| Inconsistent data quality | 9 | Automated capture | Very high |

### 7.5 Commercial Banks – Pain Points

Banks are both gatekeepers and potential partners. Their pain points must be addressed to ensure account access and settlement cooperation.

#### 7.5.1 BDC Compliance Liability

**The problem:** Banks hold accounts for licensed BDCs. If a BDC is involved in money laundering or other violations, the bank can be held liable or face reputational damage.

**Current coping mechanism:** Restrictive BDC account terms. Manual monitoring of BDC transactions. High account opening barriers.

**Cost of this pain:**

- **Reputational risk:** Association with non-compliant BDCs.  
- **Regulatory scrutiny:** Banks with many BDC accounts face more CBN attention.  
- **Operational cost:** Dedicated relationship managers for BDC accounts.

**Cuboid solution:** Cuboid provides real-time compliance monitoring and audit trails. Banks can rely on Cuboid's compliance data to reduce their own monitoring burden.

**Metric of success:** Banks offer preferential terms (lower fees, higher limits) to BDCs using Cuboid.

#### 7.5.2 Missed FX Distribution Channel

**The problem:** Banks have wholesale FX but no efficient channel to distribute small amounts to retail customers without BDCs.

**Current coping mechanism:** Ignore retail FX segment. Focus on wholesale.

**Cost of this pain:**

- **Lost revenue:** Retail FX spreads could generate significant fee income.  
- **Customer dissatisfaction:** Bank customers must go elsewhere for FX.

**Cuboid solution:** Banks can connect to Cuboid's BDC network, distributing FX through compliant BDCs while earning settlement fees.

**Metric of success:** 3+ banks partner with Cuboid for FX distribution within 18 months.

#### 7.5.3 Bank Pain Points Summary Table

| Pain Point | Severity (1-10) | Cuboid Solution | Bank Appeal |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| BDC compliance liability | 8 | Compliance monitoring | High |
| Missed FX distribution | 7 | BDC network access | Medium |

### 7.6 Fintechs & PSPs – Pain Points

Fintechs want to offer FX to their customers but lack compliant BDC partners.

#### 7.6.1 No Standardized BDC Network

**The problem:** Fintechs cannot find BDCs with consistent pricing, reliable inventory, and compliance readiness.

**Current coping mechanism:** Build own BDC relationships manually (slow, expensive) or abandon FX product.

**Cost of this pain:**

- **Lost revenue:** Cannot offer profitable FX products.  
- **Customer churn:** Customers go to competitors offering FX.

**Cuboid solution:** API access to Cuboid's BDC network. Fintechs can offer FX to their customers with one integration.

**Metric of success:** 5+ fintechs integrate Cuboid API within 18 months.

#### 7.6.2 Fintech Pain Points Summary Table

| Pain Point | Severity (1-10) | Cuboid Solution | Fintech Appeal |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| No BDC network | 9 | API access | Very high |

### 7.7 End Customers – Pain Points

Customers are the ultimate beneficiaries of an efficient FX market.

| Pain Point | Description | Cuboid Solution |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Unreliable availability | May walk to multiple BDCs before finding dollars | Brokers/BDCs on Cuboid have better inventory visibility |
| Wide price variation | Rates vary 5–10% on same street | Price transparency (brokers/BDCs can compare) |
| No receipts or proof | Handwritten receipts not accepted abroad | Digital receipts from BDC Management Module |
| Slow service | 30–45 minutes for a simple purchase | Faster trade execution via Cuboid |

### 7.8 Pain Points Cross-Reference Matrix

| Stakeholder | Top Pain | Cuboid Solution | Urgency |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Informal broker | Inventory discovery | Real-time inventory visibility | Immediate |
| Informal broker | Settlement risk | Light escrow | High |
| Licensed BDC | Compliance burden | Automated filing | Immediate |
| Licensed BDC | Inventory mismatch | Inter-BDC trading | High |
| Regulator | No visibility | Regulator dashboard | High |
| Bank | BDC liability | Compliance monitoring | Medium |
| Fintech | No BDC network | API access | Medium |
| Customer | Unreliable availability | Better inventory across network | Medium |

### 7.9 The Overlooked Stakeholder: Insane Technologies

As a 25%+ equity holder, Insane Technologies is not an external stakeholder but an internal one. Their pain points and incentives are aligned with Cuboid's success.

| Consideration | Detail |
| :---- | :---- |
| Equity stake | Minimum 25% |
| Contribution | Technical infrastructure, strategic guidance, network access |
| Expected return | Long-term value appreciation, not short-term cash |
| Risk | Cuboid failure \= wasted technical contribution |
| Incentive | Cuboid success increases value of Insane Technologies' equity |

**This alignment is rare.** Most fintechs raise from passive investors who provide only cash. Cuboid has a strategic partner providing infrastructure and expertise at no cash cost, in exchange for equity that only pays off if Cuboid wins.

### 7.10 Pain Points Validation Method

The pain points described in this section have been validated through:

1. **Informal interviews** with 25+ brokers (bank workers, independent agents) across Lagos, Kano, and Abuja, conducted with anonymity guarantees.  
2. **Interviews with 10+ BDC operators** (small, medium, and large).  
3. **Review of CBN enforcement actions** and penalty announcements (public records).  
4. **Analysis of NFIU guidance** to BDCs regarding reporting obligations.  
5. **Conversations with 3 fintech founders** who attempted to build FX products but abandoned due to BDC/broker fragmentation.  
6. **Publicly available data** on BDC license revocations and compliance fines.

---

## SECTION 8: MARKET OPPORTUNITY & SIZING (FORMAL \+ GREY MARKET)

### 8.1 The Total Addressable Market (TAM) – Corrected

Most market sizing exercises for FX in Nigeria focus only on licensed BDCs and reported CBN figures. This is like measuring an iceberg by its visible tip. The **real TAM** includes formal and grey market volume.

**TAM definition:** The total annual retail FX transaction value in Nigeria that could potentially flow through Cuboid (either as formal reported volume or grey market volume that Cuboid could make visible).

**TAM calculation approach:**

| Component | Estimated Annual Volume (USD) | Data Source |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| CBN official FX inflow (all sources) | $30B – $40B | CBN annual reports |
| Less: Wholesale/interbank (not retail) | ($15B – $20B) | Estimated |
| **Retail-eligible volume** | **$15B – $20B** | Derived |
| Licensed BDCs reported volume | $5B – $8B | CBN BDC returns |
| Unreported BDC volume | $2B – $4B | Broker interviews, triangulation |
| Informal broker volume (bank workers) | $6B – $10B | Broker interviews |
| Informal broker volume (independent) | $3B – $5B | Broker interviews |
| Corporate treasury diversion | $2B – $4B | Industry sources |
| **Total retail FX TAM** | **$18B – $31B** | **Cuboid estimate** |

**The key insight:** The grey market (informal brokers, unreported BDC volume, corporate diversion) is approximately **2–3 times larger** than the formal reported BDC market. A platform that captures only formal BDCs misses most of the opportunity.

### 8.2 Serviceable Addressable Market (SAM)

**SAM definition:** The portion of TAM that Cuboid can realistically address within the first 3 years, given operational, regulatory, and partnership constraints.

**SAM calculation:**

| Component | Year 1 | Year 2 | Year 3 |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Formal BDCs (reported volume) | $5B – $8B | $5B – $8B | $5B – $8B |
| % of formal BDCs likely to adopt Cuboid (cumulative) | 2–5% | 10–15% | 20–30% |
| **Formal BDC addressable volume** | **$100M – $400M** | **$500M – $1.2B** | **$1B – $2.4B** |
| Informal broker volume (total) | $9B – $15B | $9B – $15B | $9B – $15B |
| % of broker volume Cuboid can influence (via BDC bridge) | 1–3% | 5–10% | 10–20% |
| **Informal broker addressable volume** | **$90M – $450M** | **$450M – $1.5B** | **$900M – $3B** |
| **Total SAM (volume)** | **$190M – $850M** | **$950M – $2.7B** | **$1.9B – $5.4B** |

**SAM is not TAM.** Cuboid will not capture all FX volume. But capturing even 10% of SAM in Year 3 represents $190M – $540M in annual transaction volume flowing through the platform.

### 8.3 Serviceable Obtainable Market (SOM)

**SOM definition:** The portion of SAM that Cuboid can realistically capture given current resources ($5,500 funding, Insane Technologies contribution, lean team).

**SOM calculation (conservative):**

| Component | Year 1 | Year 2 | Year 3 |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Total SAM volume | $190M – $850M | $950M – $2.7B | $1.9B – $5.4B |
| Cuboid capture rate (% of SAM) | 0.5–1% | 2–5% | 5–10% |
| **SOM volume (USD)** | **$1M – $8.5M** | **$19M – $135M** | **$95M – $540M** |

**Even the conservative estimate is substantial:** $1 million in transaction volume in Year 1, growing to nearly $100 million by Year 3—with only $5,500 initial funding.

### 8.4 Revenue Opportunity Mapping

Cuboid's revenue is a function of transaction volume and fee rates.

| Revenue Stream | Fee Rate | Year 1 Volume (SOM) | Year 1 Revenue | Year 3 Volume (SOM) | Year 3 Revenue |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Transaction fees (broker-BDC) | 0.1–0.3% | $500k – $4M | $500 – $12,000 | $50M – $300M | $50k – $900k |
| BDC Management Module | $20–$100/month | 5–10 BDCs | $1,200 – $12,000 | 200–500 BDCs | $48k – $600k |
| Broker referral fees (from BDC subs) | 10% of BDC sub | 5 BDCs referred | $120 – $600 | 100 BDCs referred | $1,200 – $6,000 |
| Compliance-as-a-Service (BDCs) | $10–$30/month | 5–10 BDCs | $600 – $3,600 | 200–500 BDCs | $24k – $180k |
| Inter-BDC trading spread | 0.05–0.1% | $100k – $500k | $50 – $500 | $10M – $50M | $5k – $50k |
| API access (fintechs, banks) | $500–$2,000/month | 0 | $0 | 3–5 partners | $18k – $120k |
| **Total annual revenue (conservative)** |  |  | **$2,500 – $28,700** |  | **$146k – $1.86M** |

**At moderate adoption (midpoint of ranges):**

| Year | Monthly Volume | Annual Revenue | Profitability |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | $4M | $15,000 | Loss (investment) |
| 2 | $75M | $300,000 | Breakeven to small profit |
| 3 | $300M | $1,000,000 | Profitable |

### 8.5 Market Drivers (Why Growth Will Accelerate)

| Driver | Impact | Timing |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| CBN FX reforms | Increased pressure on BDCs to formalize and report | Now – 2026 |
| NFIU enforcement | Greater scrutiny of BDC compliance; fines increase | Now – 2025 |
| Bank de-risking | Banks closing accounts of informal brokers; pushes them to formal channels | 2024 – 2026 |
| Diaspora remittances | $20B+ annual inflow needs conversion to Naira; BDCs and brokers are channels | Continuous |
| Naira volatility | Customers need reliable FX access more than ever | Continuous |
| Fintech demand | PSPs and neobanks want to offer FX; need BDC/broker partners | Now – 2025 |

### 8.6 Geographic Segmentation

Cuboid will launch in Lagos (highest density of brokers and BDCs), then expand.

| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Lagos | 1,500 – 2,000 | 8,000 – 12,000 | $8B – $12B | 1 (Month 1\) |

| Ibadan | 200 – 300 | 1,000 – 1,500 | $500M – $1B | 3 (Month 7\) |
| Other cities | 1,500 – 2,000 | 3,000 – 5,000 | $2B – $5B | 4 (Month 10+) |

### 8.7 Competitive Landscape (Broker-Aware)

Most competitors ignore brokers. This is Cuboid's advantage.

| Competitor | Focus | Broker Awareness | Weakness |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| FMDQ (formal FX exchange) | Wholesale, institutional | None | Not retail, not BDC/broker friendly |
| Bank-provided BDC portals | BDC reporting only | None | No trading, no broker appeal |
| Custom software vendors (e.g., Finacle) | Enterprise BDCs | None | Expensive, no network effects |
| WhatsApp trading groups | Informal brokers | Yes (but no product) | No tools, no compliance, no escrow |
| Competitor fintechs (e.g., Chipper FX) | Consumer-facing | None | Bypass BDCs/brokers; regulatory risk |

**Cuboid's unique position:** The only platform that explicitly acknowledges brokers as primary movers, builds tools they will use, and maintains regulatory defensibility through licensed counterparty requirements and compliance ladder.

### 8.8 Market Risks (Broker-Aware)

| Risk | Likelihood | Impact | Mitigation |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Regulator shuts down platform for facilitating unlicensed activity | Low | High | Terms of service; licensed counterparty requirement; proactive regulator engagement |
| Brokers refuse to adopt digital tools | Medium | High | Build for their workflow; WhatsApp integration; free pilot |
| BDCs refuse to work with brokers | Low | Medium | Show BDCs volume opportunity; broker demand feed |
| Banks block settlements | Medium | High | Partner with banks early; compliance monitoring |
| Competitor launches similar product | Medium | Medium | Move fast; Insane Technologies infrastructure advantage |

### 8.9 Summary: The Opportunity Size in One Page

| Metric | Conservative | Moderate | Optimistic |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Total retail FX TAM (Nigeria) | $18B | $25B | $31B |
| Cuboid SAM (Year 3\) | $1.9B | $3.5B | $5.4B |
| Cuboid SOM (Year 3 volume) | $95M | $300M | $540M |
| Cuboid Year 3 revenue | $146k | $500k | $1.86M |
| Investment required (this round) | $5,500 | $5,500 | $5,500 |
| ROI (Year 3 revenue / investment) | 26x | 90x | 338x |

**The conclusion:** Even the most conservative projections show that a $5,500 investment (with Insane Technologies' 25%+ equity contribution) can build a platform that addresses a multi-billion-dollar market. The grey market is not a problem to be eliminated—it is an opportunity to be captured.

## SECTION 9: SOLUTION OVERVIEW – THE CUBOID FRAMEWORK (BROKER-COMPATIBLE)

### 9.1 The Cuboid Framework: Three Dimensions, Two Modes

Cuboid is not a single product. It is a **framework** with three core dimensions, each operating in two modes—one for formal participants (licensed BDCs, regulators, banks) and one for informal participants (brokers) that maintains regulatory defensibility.

**The three dimensions:**

| Dimension | Description | Formal Mode (BDC/Regulator) | Informal Mode (Broker) |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **Technology** | Digital tools for trading, settlement, and management | Full feature set: inter-BDC trading, automated compliance, API | Light feature set: chat-to-trade, quote generation, customer management |
| **Compliance** | Automated reporting, audit trails, regulator visibility | Full reporting to CBN/NFIU, real-time dashboard | Activity logged, visible to regulators upon request, nudges toward formalization |
| **Ecosystem** | Network connecting all participants | BDC-to-BDC, BDC-to-bank, BDC-to-fintech | Broker-to-BDC (broker-to-broker prohibited), referral pathways |

**The unifying principle:** Every actual FX trade on Cuboid must involve at least one licensed BDC on at least one side. Brokers cannot trade anonymously with other brokers. This single rule maintains regulatory defensibility while allowing brokers to use the platform for sourcing, quoting, and customer management.

### 9.2 High-Level Architecture Diagram (Text Description)

┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐

│                           CUBOID PLATFORM                                    │

├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤

│                                                                              │

│  ┌───────────────────┐    ┌───────────────────┐    ┌───────────────────┐   │

│  │   BROKER MODE     │    │    BDC MODE       │    │  REGULATOR MODE   │   │

│  ├───────────────────┤    ├───────────────────┤    ├───────────────────┤   │

│  │ • Chat-to-trade   │    │ • Inventory mgmt  │    │ • Dashboard       │   │

│  │ • Quote generator │    │ • Customer mgmt   │    │ • Audit viewer    │   │

│  │ • Customer list   │    │ • Digital receipts│    │ • Anonymized flow │   │

│  │ • Light escrow    │    │ • Inter-BDC trade │    │ • Suspicious alert│   │

│  │ • BDC discovery   │    │ • Compliance auto │    │ • Data export     │   │

│  └─────────┬─────────┘    └─────────┬─────────┘    └─────────┬─────────┘   │

│            │                        │                        │             │

│            ▼                        ▼                        ▼             │

│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐   │

│  │                      CORE ENGINE (Shared)                           │   │

│  ├─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤   │

│  │ • User registry (roles: broker, BDC, regulator, bank, fintech)     │   │

│  │ • KYB/KYC (tiered by role and verification level)                  │   │

│  │ • Trade matching engine (BDC-BDC, BDC-broker)                      │   │

│  │ • Ledger (non-custodial, transaction logging)                      │   │

│  │ • Settlement tracking (bank transfer confirmations)                │   │

│  │ • Escrow (light, for broker-BDC trades)                            │   │

│  │ • Audit trail (immutable, all actions logged)                      │   │

│  │ • Compliance engine (report generation, nudge engine)              │   │

│  └─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘   │

│            │                        │                        │             │

│            ▼                        ▼                        ▼             │

│  ┌───────────────────┐    ┌───────────────────┐    ┌───────────────────┐   │

│  │   EXTERNAL API    │    │  BANK INTEGRATION │    │  REGULATOR API    │   │

│  ├───────────────────┤    ├───────────────────┤    ├───────────────────┤   │

│  │ • Fintechs        │    │ • Account         │    │ • goAML (future)  │   │

│  │ • PSPs            │    │   verification    │    │ • CBN (future)    │   │

│  │ • Banks (read)    │    │ • Settlement      │    │ • Data pull       │   │

│  └───────────────────┘    └───────────────────┘    └───────────────────┘   │

│                                                                              │

└─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

### 9.3 The Compliance Ladder (Core Innovation)

The most important design element of Cuboid is the **Compliance Ladder**—a structured pathway that allows any user to move from anonymous/unverified to fully licensed at their own pace.

**The ladder visualized:**

RUNG 5: Fully Licensed BDC

│       • Full platform access

│       • Inter-BDC trading

│       • Regulator dashboard (opt-in)

│       • API access

│       • Compliance reporting automated

│

RUNG 4: Partnered with Licensed BDC

│       • Trades executed under BDC umbrella

│       • Higher transaction limits

│       • Compliance covered by partner BDC

│       • Revenue share with BDC

│

RUNG 3: Verified Individual (ID Uploaded)

│       • Light escrow available

│       • Can send trade requests to BDCs

│       • Customer management

│       • Quote generation

│       • Nudges toward partnership

│

RUNG 2: Registered User (Phone Number)

│       • Basic customer list

│       • Quote generation (limited)

│       • Can view BDC inventory (anonymized)

│       • Cannot execute trades

│

RUNG 1: Anonymous Browser

│       • View public rates

│       • Read documentation

│       • No platform features

│

RUNG 0: Not on Platform

**How users move up:**

| Transition | Trigger | Benefit |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Rung 1 → 2 | Provide phone number, accept terms | Access to basic tools |
| Rung 2 → 3 | Upload government ID, selfie verification | Light escrow, trade requests |
| Rung 3 → 4 | Partner with a licensed BDC on platform | Higher limits, compliance coverage |
| Rung 4 → 5 | Obtain BDC license or convert existing license | Full control, no partner split |

**Crucially:** Cuboid never forces users to move up. The nudges are informative, not punitive. "You've completed 50 trade requests. Here's how partnering with a BDC could increase your limits and reduce your risk."

### 9.4 Two-Mode Product Design: Broker Mode vs BDC Mode

The same platform presents different interfaces and features depending on the user's declared role and verification level.

#### 9.4.1 Broker Mode (For Informal Brokers)

**Target user:** Bank worker, independent agent, or corporate treasury contact operating informally.

**Interface style:** WhatsApp-inspired, mobile-first, minimal text, big buttons, fast.

**Core features:**

| Feature | Description | Why Broker Adopts |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Chat-to-trade | Type "need $5k USD for school fees" → system suggests available BDCs with rates | Eliminates phone calls |
| Quick quote | Generate professional quote with expiry time, send via WhatsApp | Looks professional, saves time |
| Customer list | Store names, contact info, past requests, notes | Never forget a customer |
| BDC inventory feed | See which BDCs in area have USD and at what rate | Finds sources instantly |
| Light escrow | Customer funds held; released when USD confirmed | Eliminates settlement risk |
| Transaction history | All past trades logged | Audit trail, repeat customer insights |
| Referral dashboard | Track referrals of BDCs to Cuboid, see earnings | Passive income |

**What broker mode does NOT have:**

- Inter-broker trading (broker-to-broker anonymous trading prohibited)  
- Automated compliance filing (brokers are not licensed)  
- Regulator dashboard access  
- API access

#### 9.4.2 BDC Mode (For Licensed BDCs)

**Target user:** Licensed BDC operators, compliance officers, cashiers.

**Interface style:** Dashboard-oriented, desktop-friendly (mobile responsive), data-rich.

**Core features:**

| Feature | Description | Why BDC Adopts |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Inventory management | Real-time USD/NGN/other holdings across branches | Know position instantly |
| Customer management | KYC storage, transaction history, preferences | Serve repeat customers |
| Digital receipts | CBN-compliant receipts with QR code | Audit-ready, professional |
| Inter-BDC trading | See other BDCs' excess/deficit, execute peer trades | Balance inventory |
| Broker demand feed | See trade requests from brokers in area | New revenue channel |
| Compliance automation | Auto-generate CBN/NFIU reports, one-click filing | Save hours, avoid fines |
| Settlement tracking | Track incoming/outgoing payments | Reduce settlement risk |
| Regulator dashboard (opt-in) | Share real-time data with CBN/NFIU | Build regulator trust |

**What BDC mode has that broker mode does NOT:**

- Inter-BDC trading  
- Compliance automation (filing)  
- Regulator dashboard  
- API access (for fintech/bank integration)

### 9.5 How a Trade Flows Through Cuboid (Three Scenarios)

#### Scenario 1: Broker to BDC Trade (Most Common)

| Step | Actor | Action | System Response |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | Broker | Types "need $3k USD for medical fees" in chat-to-trade | Parses request: $3k, USD, medical purpose |
| 2 | System | Matches request with BDCs in broker's area that have USD available | Shows 3 BDCs with rates, distances |
| 3 | Broker | Selects a BDC, accepts quoted rate | Creates trade request to BDC |
| 4 | BDC | Receives notification, confirms inventory available | Accepts trade, locks inventory |
| 5 | Customer | Sends naira to broker (or directly to escrow) | System tracks payment (manual confirmation initially) |
| 6 | Escrow (light) | Holds customer funds | Status: "Funds received, awaiting USD delivery" |
| 7 | Broker | Sends naira to BDC (or BDC already has naira from previous step) | System tracks |
| 8 | BDC | Confirms USD delivery to customer | System releases escrow to broker |
| 9 | System | Logs trade, generates compliance record | Audit trail complete |

**Total time (target):** 5–15 minutes.

#### Scenario 2: BDC to BDC Trade (Inventory Balancing)

| Step | Actor | Action | System Response |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | BDC (excess) | Posts "selling $20k USD at NGN 760" | Listed in inter-BDC market |
| 2 | BDC (deficit) | Views inventory feed, sees offer | Accepts offer |
| 3 | System | Matches, creates trade | Locks inventory |
| 4 | BDC (deficit) | Sends naira to BDC (excess) | System tracks |
| 5 | BDC (excess) | Confirms naira received, sends USD | System tracks |
| 6 | System | Logs trade, generates compliance record for both BDCs | Audit trail complete |

**Total time (target):** 2–10 minutes.

#### Scenario 3: Broker to Broker (Prohibited)

**Cuboid does not allow broker-to-broker anonymous trading.** Brokers can only trade with licensed BDCs. This is a hard rule, enforced by the system. Any attempt to match two brokers without a BDC on one side is rejected.

**Rationale:** Broker-to-broker trading would make Cuboid a platform for unlicensed FX dealing, unacceptable to regulators. Requiring a licensed BDC on every trade provides regulatory defensibility.

### 9.6 The Broker Bridge: Features That Attract Without Endorsing

Cuboid walks a careful line: build features brokers want, but do not explicitly market to them as a trading platform.

**Features brokers will discover and love (without being told):**

| Feature | How Broker Discovers | Why They Stay |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Quick quote generation | Tries "quote" button, sees professional output | Saves time, looks professional |
| Customer list | Adds first customer, sees history populate | Never forgets a customer |
| BDC inventory feed | Searches for USD, sees available BDCs | Finds sources instantly |
| Light escrow | Uses it once, avoids a failed trade | Eliminates risk |
| Referral earnings | Refers a BDC, sees commission appear | Passive income |

**What Cuboid will NOT do:**

- Advertise to brokers as "trade FX without a license"  
- Send push notifications encouraging unlicensed trading  
- Hide broker activity from regulators  
- Allow broker-to-broker anonymous trading

**The legal line:** Cuboid is a productivity tool for customer management, quote generation, and connecting with licensed financial institutions (BDCs). Brokers may use it for more, but that is against terms of service. Cuboid maintains audit trails and shares data with regulators upon request.

### 9.7 The BDC Management Module as the Formal Anchor

While brokers drive volume, licensed BDCs provide the compliance anchor. The BDC Management Module is the product that makes Cuboid regulator-friendly.

**BDC Management Module features (detailed in Section 12):**

| Feature | Compliance Value | Revenue Value |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Inventory management | Real-time position visibility | Core subscription feature |
| Customer KYC | Audit-ready records | Core subscription feature |
| Digital receipts | Proof of transaction | Core subscription feature |
| Inter-BDC trading | Trades between licensed entities only | Transaction fees |
| Compliance automation | Auto-filing to CBN/NFIU | Add-on fee |
| Broker demand feed | New revenue channel | No extra fee (BDC subscription includes) |

**Pricing:** $20–$100 per month depending on volume and features.

### 9.8 The Insane Technologies Contribution

Insane Technologies (minimum 25% equity) provides the technical foundation that makes building Cuboid for $5,500 possible.

| Component | Provided By | Replacement Cost |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Authentication (signup, login, roles) | Insane Technologies | $5,000 – $10,000 |
| Chat infrastructure (real-time messaging) | Insane Technologies | $10,000 – $15,000 |
| Basic ledger (transaction logging) | Insane Technologies | $3,000 – $5,000 |
| User registry (roles, permissions) | Insane Technologies | $2,000 – $4,000 |
| API scaffolding | Insane Technologies | $3,000 – $6,000 |
| Hosting credits (AWS, Firebase) | Insane Technologies | $2,000 – $5,000 |
| **Total value contributed** |  | **$25,000 – $45,000** |

**In exchange:** Minimum 25% equity. This is not a typical investment—it is a strategic partnership where technology is the contribution.

### 9.9 What the MVP Includes (First $5,500)

The Minimum Viable Product (MVP) will include the following, prioritized for broker adoption and BDC participation.

| Feature | Included in MVP? | Why |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| User registration (phone number) | Yes | Essential for all users |
| Broker mode: chat-to-trade (basic) | Yes | Primary broker adoption driver |
| Broker mode: quote generation | Yes | Quick win for brokers |
| Broker mode: customer list | Yes | Retention feature |
| Broker mode: BDC inventory feed (view only) | Yes | Value for brokers |
| Broker mode: light escrow (manual confirmation) | Yes | Settlement risk reduction |
| BDC mode: inventory management (basic) | Yes | Core BDC feature |
| BDC mode: inter-BDC trading (manual matching) | Yes | Inventory balancing |
| BDC mode: digital receipts (basic) | Yes | BDC compliance need |
| Compliance ladder (nudges) | Partial (Rungs 1-3 only) | Future: Rungs 4-5 |
| Compliance automation (auto-filing) | No (MVP manual export) | Phase 2 |
| Regulator dashboard | No (MVP internal only) | Phase 2 |
| API for fintechs | No | Phase 3 |

**What the MVP will NOT have (deferred):**

- Automated CBN/NFIU filing (Phase 2\)  
- Real-time regulator dashboard (Phase 2\)  
- API for fintech integration (Phase 3\)  
- Advanced analytics (Phase 3\)

**The MVP is intentionally minimal:** Enough to prove broker adoption and BDC participation, not enough to be a full compliance solution. Phase 2 adds compliance features (funded by early revenue or seed round).

### 9.10 Development Philosophy (Broker-First, Then Compliance)

Cuboid's development roadmap inverts typical fintech priorities.

| Priority | Typical Fintech | Cuboid |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | Compliance features | Broker adoption features |
| 2 | Regulator reporting | BDC management features |
| 3 | BDC tools | Compliance features |
| 4 | User experience | Regulator reporting |

**Rationale:** A platform with perfect compliance but no users is worthless. Cuboid focuses first on features that make brokers and BDCs *want* to use the platform. Compliance is added incrementally, with the understanding that early users are informed that audit trails exist and data may be shared with regulators.

**The risk:** This approach could be seen as prioritizing growth over compliance. Cuboid mitigates by:

- Maintaining audit trails from Day 1  
- Including terms of service that prohibit unlicensed trading  
- Requiring a licensed BDC on every trade  
- Engaging regulators early (by Month 6\)

### 9.11 Summary: The Cuboid Framework

| Element | Description |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Core innovation** | Compliance ladder – structured pathway from informal to licensed |
| **Two modes** | Broker mode (productivity) \+ BDC mode (compliance & management) |
| **Hard rule** | Every trade involves at least one licensed BDC |
| **Broker appeal** | Chat-to-trade, quick quotes, customer management, light escrow |
| **BDC value** | Inventory management, inter-BDC trading, compliance automation, broker demand |
| **Regulator defense** | Audit trails, licensed counterparty requirement, proactive dashboard (future) |
| **Technical foundation** | Insane Technologies (25%+ equity) provides $25k–$45k in infrastructure |
| **MVP cost** | $5,500 (strategic round) |
| **Phase 2 funding** | Early revenue or $50k–$100k seed round |

---

## SECTION 10: CORE PLATFORM MODULES

### 10.1 Module Overview

Cuboid is built as a set of interconnected modules. This modularity allows:

- Different user types to see only relevant features  
- Phased development (MVP first, then add modules)  
- Potential to sell modules separately (e.g., BDC Management Module as standalone)

**Module map:**

| Module | Primary Users | Phase | Revenue Model |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| User & Identity Management | All | Phase 1 (MVP) | Free (enables others) |
| Chat-to-Trade Engine | Brokers | Phase 1 (MVP) | Transaction fees |
| Quote Generator | Brokers | Phase 1 (MVP) | Free (drives volume) |
| Customer Management | Brokers, BDCs | Phase 1 (MVP) | Included in BDC subscription |
| Inventory Management | BDCs | Phase 1 (MVP) | BDC subscription |
| Inter-BDC Trading | BDCs | Phase 1 (MVP) | Transaction fees \+ spread |
| Light Escrow | Brokers, BDCs | Phase 1 (MVP) | Transaction fees |
| Digital Receipts | BDCs | Phase 1 (MVP) | BDC subscription |
| Compliance Ladder Engine | All | Phase 1 (MVP \- Rungs 1-3) | Free (conversion tool) |
| Compliance Automation (Filing) | BDCs | Phase 2 | Add-on fee |
| Regulator Dashboard | Regulators | Phase 2 | Free (regulator goodwill) |
| API Gateway | Fintechs, Banks | Phase 3 | API access fees |

### 10.2 Module 1: User & Identity Management

**Purpose:** Register, verify, and manage all platform users with role-based access control.

**Features:**

| Feature | Description | MVP? |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Phone number registration | Simple OTP-based signup | Yes |
| Role selection (broker, BDC, regulator) | User declares role | Yes |
| KYB for BDCs | Upload license, CAC documents, director IDs | Yes |
| ID verification for brokers (optional, Rung 3\) | Upload government ID, selfie | Yes (Phase 1b) |
| Role-based permissions | Brokers see broker features, BDCs see BDC features | Yes |
| Multi-factor authentication | Optional for BDCs | Yes |
| Session management | Login history, device tracking | Yes |

**Verification tiers (for compliance ladder):**

| Tier | Requirements | Access Level |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 0 (Anonymous) | None | View public content only |
| 1 (Registered) | Phone number | Basic broker/BDC features |
| 2 (Verified individual) | ID upload, selfie | Light escrow, trade requests |
| 3 (Business verified) | CAC, license (for BDCs) | Full BDC features |
| 4 (Partnered) | Association with licensed BDC | BDC umbrella trading |

### 10.3 Module 2: Chat-to-Trade Engine

**Purpose:** Allow brokers to request FX using natural language, similar to WhatsApp.

**How it works:**

| Step | User Action | System Response |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | Broker types: "need $5k USD for school fees" | NLP parses amount ($5k), currency (USD), purpose (school fees) |
| 2 | System checks available BDCs in broker's area | Returns list: BDC A (NGN 760, 2km), BDC B (NGN 765, 5km) |
| 3 | Broker selects BDC, accepts rate | Creates trade request |
| 4 | BDC receives notification, confirms | Trade locked |

**NLP capabilities (MVP):**

| Intent | Example | Parses |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Buy USD | "need $3k USD" | Amount, currency (USD), direction (buy) |
| Sell USD | "selling $2k USD" | Amount, currency (USD), direction (sell) |
| Check rate | "what's dollar rate" | Returns current best rates from BDCs |
| Customer request | "Mr John needs $1k for medicals" | Creates customer record, trade request |

**Why this matters for brokers:** Currently, brokers manually type these messages to multiple contacts. Cuboid automates the distribution and response collection.

### 10.4 Module 3: Quote Generator

**Purpose:** Allow brokers (or BDCs) to generate professional-looking rate quotes to send to customers.

**Quote output includes:**

| Field | Example |
| :---- | :---- |
| Broker/BDC name | "John's FX Services" |
| Date and time | "15 Jan 2025, 10:32 AM" |
| Quote expiry | "Valid until 11:00 AM today" |
| Amount | "$3,000 USD" |
| Exchange rate | "1 USD \= NGN 762" |
| Total naira | "NGN 2,286,000" |
| Purpose (optional) | "School fees" |
| QR code (if BDC) | Links to transaction record |
| Terms | "Subject to fund confirmation" |

**Why this matters:** Customers perceive professional quotes as more trustworthy. Brokers using Cubido can send quotes that look like they come from a formal business, increasing customer confidence.

### 10.5 Module 4: Customer Management

**Purpose:** Allow brokers and BDCs to store and manage customer information.

**Data fields:**

| Field | Type | Used By |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Name | Text | Brokers, BDCs |
| Phone number | Text | Brokers, BDCs |
| Email (optional) | Text | Brokers, BDCs |
| Customer type | Individual/Business | BDCs (KYC) |
| ID type and number | Text | BDCs (KYC required) |
| Transaction history | List of past trades | Brokers, BDCs |
| Preferred currency | USD/GBP/EUR | Brokers, BDCs |
| Notes | Free text | Brokers only (not compliance-sensitive) |
| Trust score (internal) | 0-100 | Brokers, BDCs |

**Why this matters for brokers:** "I have 500 customers in my phone but I don't know who asked for what." Customer management solves this.

**Why this matters for BDCs:** KYC is a regulatory requirement. Digital storage is audit-ready.

### 10.6 Module 5: Inventory Management

**Purpose:** Allow BDCs (and optionally brokers) to track their FX holdings in real time.

**Features:**

| Feature | Description | BDCs | Brokers |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Multi-currency balances | USD, NGN, GBP, EUR | Yes | Yes (but limited) |
| Real-time updates | Automatic when trades occur | Yes | Manual entry (MVP) |
| Branch-level tracking | Separate balances per branch | Yes | No |
| Low inventory alerts | Notification when below threshold | Yes | No |
| Excess inventory alerts | Notification when idle above threshold | Yes | No |
| Historical position | View past balances by date | Yes | No |

**Why this matters:** Most BDCs track inventory on Excel or paper. Real-time digital tracking eliminates manual errors and provides instant visibility.

### 10.7 Module 6: Inter-BDC Trading

**Purpose:** Allow licensed BDCs to trade with each other to balance inventory.

**How it works:**

| Step | Action |
| :---- | :---- |
| 1 | BDC with excess USD posts: "Selling $20k USD at NGN 760" |
| 2 | BDC with deficit views market feed, sees offer |
| 3 | Deficit BDC accepts offer (or counter-offers) |
| 4 | System creates trade, locks inventory from both sides |
| 5 | Deficit BDC sends naira (tracked manually or via bank API) |
| 6 | Excess BDC confirms naira received, sends USD |
| 7 | Trade marked complete, compliance record generated |

**Why this matters:** Currently, BDCs call each other to find trades. This is slow, inefficient, and limited to personal networks. Inter-BDC trading on Cubido is instant and visible to all BDCs on the platform.

### 10.8 Module 7: Light Escrow

**Purpose:** Reduce settlement risk for broker-BDC trades.

**How it works:**

| Role | Without Escrow | With Light Escrow |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Customer | Pays broker; risks broker failing to deliver | Pays into escrow; money held until USD confirmed |
| Broker | Receives customer funds; risks source failing | Funds held; no risk of losing customer money |
| BDC | Receives naira from broker; may not have USD | Confirms USD before escrow release |

**Escrow flow:**

1. Customer sends naira to escrow account (virtual account or designated bank account).  
2. System confirms receipt, notifies broker and BDC.  
3. BDC delivers USD (or confirms delivery).  
4. Customer confirms receipt (or BDC provides proof).  
5. System releases naira from escrow to broker (or BDC, depending on trade structure).

**Note:** True escrow requires a bank partner or payment service provider. In MVP, escrow is "light" – manual confirmation of transfers rather than automated holding. Phase 2 will integrate with a payment partner for true escrow.

### 10.9 Module 8: Digital Receipts

**Purpose:** Generate CBN-compliant receipts for BDC transactions.

**Receipt includes (CBN requirements):**

| Field | Required by CBN |
| :---- | :---- |
| BDC name and license number | Yes |
| Customer name and ID number | Yes |
| Date and time | Yes |
| Currency pair (USD/NGN) | Yes |
| Amount (foreign currency and naira equivalent) | Yes |
| Exchange rate used | Yes |
| Purpose of transaction (coded) | Yes |
| QR code linking to transaction record | Recommended |

**Why this matters:** BDCs are required to issue receipts. Many use handwritten or simple printed receipts that do not meet CBN standards. Digital receipts from Cuboid are automatically compliant.

### 10.10 Module 9: Compliance Ladder Engine

**Purpose:** Nudge users toward formalization without forcing them.

**How it works:**

| User Action | Nudge Trigger | Nudge Message |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Completes 10 trade requests | Automatic | "You've completed 10 trade requests. Did you know? Partnering with a BDC increases your limits and reduces risk." |
| Reaches $50k total volume | Automatic | "You've moved over $50k in volume. Formalizing your status could open higher limits and better rates." |
| Uses platform for 30 days | Email/SMS | "30 days on Cuboid\! Here's how to take the next step." |
| Clicks "partner with BDC" | User-initiated | Shows list of BDCs accepting partners in their area |

**What the ladder does NOT do:** Block users who remain at lower rungs. The goal is conversion through value demonstration, not coercion.

### 10.11 Module 10: Compliance Automation (Phase 2\)

**Purpose:** Automatically generate and file CBN/NFIU reports for BDCs.

**Reports generated:**

| Report | Frequency | Destination |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Daily returns | Daily | CBN |
| Weekly positions | Weekly | CBN |
| Currency transaction reports (CTRs) | Real-time | NFIU (goAML) |
| Suspicious transaction reports (STRs) | As needed | NFIU (goAML) |

**How it works:** Trade data is captured once at execution. The compliance engine formats it according to CBN/NFIU templates. BDC reviews (optional) and clicks "submit" or API pushes automatically.

**Why this matters:** BDCs spend 10–20 hours per week on compliance filing. Cuboid reduces this to minutes.

### 10.12 Module 11: Regulator Dashboard (Phase 2\)

**Purpose:** Provide CBN and NFIU with real-time visibility into platform activity.

**Dashboard features (anonymized by default):**

| Feature | Description |
| :---- | :---- |
| Total volume (daily/weekly/monthly) | Aggregated across all BDCs |
| Geographic distribution | Volume by city, state |
| Rate trends | Average rates over time |
| BDC compliance scores | % of BDCs filing on time |
| Suspicious activity alerts | Flagged transactions (anonymized initially) |
| Drill-down (with authorization) | Individual BDC or broker data upon request |

**Why this matters:** Regulators currently have no real-time visibility. Cuboid offers a solution that respects privacy while providing oversight.

### 10.13 Module 12: API Gateway (Phase 3\)

**Purpose:** Allow fintechs, banks, and PSPs to programmatically access Cuboid's BDC network.

**API endpoints (planned):**

| Endpoint | Method | Purpose |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| `/rates` | GET | Get current best rates from BDCs |
| `/quote` | POST | Request a quote for a specific amount |
| `/trade` | POST | Execute a trade (requires pre-approved BDC partner) |
| `/status` | GET | Check trade status |
| `/history` | GET | Retrieve transaction history (for BDC) |

**Pricing:** Tiered based on volume. $500–$2,000 per month plus per-transaction fee.

**Why this matters:** Fintechs want to offer FX but lack BDC partners. Cuboid provides a single API to a network of compliant BDCs.

### 10.14 Module Integration Summary

| User Journey | Modules Used |
| :---- | :---- |
| Broker discovers Cuboid, signs up | User & Identity Management |
| Broker chats "need $5k USD" | Chat-to-Trade Engine |
| Broker sends quote to customer | Quote Generator |
| Broker saves customer for next time | Customer Management |
| Broker finds BDC with inventory | Inventory Management (BDC view) |
| Trade executed with escrow | Light Escrow |
| BDC records the trade | Inventory Management, Digital Receipts |
| BDC files compliance report | Compliance Automation (Phase 2\) |
| Regulator views aggregated data | Regulator Dashboard (Phase 2\) |
| Fintech integrates FX into their app | API Gateway (Phase 3\) |

---

**End of Section 9 and Section 10**

I have now completed **Section 9 (Solution Overview – The Cuboid Framework – Broker-Compatible)** and **Section 10 (Core Platform Modules)**.

Shall I proceed with **Section 11 (GTM & Compliance Module – Strategic Partners \+ BDCs)** and **Section 12 (BDC Management Module – Sellable to Partners)** next?

Here are **Section 11** and **Section 12** of the Cuboid Business Concept Note, fully rewritten with the broker-aware context. Formatted for Google Docs copy-paste.
