### 18.3 Technology Stack (Insane Technologies \+ Open Source)

| Layer | Technology | Provider | Phase |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **Frontend (Web)** | React.js (or Vue.js) with Tailwind CSS | Open source \+ custom | MVP |
| **Mobile** | PWA (Progressive Web App) – no app store initially | Open source | MVP |
| **API Gateway** | Express.js \+ custom middleware | Insane Technologies | MVP |
| **Authentication** | JWT-based, OTP via SMS/WhatsApp (Twilio) | Insane Technologies \+ Twilio | MVP |
| **Chat Infrastructure** | WebSockets (Socket.io or similar) | Insane Technologies | MVP |
| **Database** | PostgreSQL (Supabase or AWS RDS) | Open source \+ cloud provider | MVP |
| **Cache** | Redis (Upstash or AWS ElastiCache) | Open source | Phase 2 |
| **Object Storage** | AWS S3 or Cloudflare R2 | Cloud provider | MVP |
| **Background Jobs** | Bull (Redis) or AWS SQS | Open source | Phase 2 |
| **Hosting** | AWS (EC2, Lambda) or Vercel/Railway | Cloud provider | MVP |
| **Audit Logs** | Immutable storage (AWS S3 with Object Lock) | Cloud provider | MVP |

**Total monthly hosting cost (MVP):** $50 – $150 (within $5,500 funding for first 6-12 months via credits).

### 18.4 Insane Technologies Contribution – Technical Details

| Component | Provided By | Description | Replacement Cost |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| User authentication | Insane Technologies | Signup, login, OTP, role management, session handling | $5,000 – $8,000 |
| Role-based access control | Insane Technologies | Permissions for broker, BDC, regulator, admin | $2,000 – $4,000 |
| Real-time chat engine | Insane Technologies | WebSocket-based messaging for chat-to-trade | $8,000 – $12,000 |
| Basic ledger | Insane Technologies | Double-entry transaction logging, balance tracking | $3,000 – $5,000 |
| API scaffolding | Insane Technologies | Routes, middleware, error handling, logging | $3,000 – $6,000 |
| Notification service | Insane Technologies | SMS, email, in-app notifications | $2,000 – $4,000 |
| Infrastructure templates | Insane Technologies | IaC (Terraform/CloudFormation) for deployment | $2,000 – $6,000 |
| **Total contributed value** |  |  | **$25,000 – $45,000** |

**In exchange:** Minimum 25% equity. This is not a typical investment – it is a strategic technology partnership.

### 18.5 Build vs Buy Decisions (MVP)

| Feature | Build | Buy | Decision | Rationale |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Authentication | Insane Tech | – | Build (provided) | Already available |
| Chat engine | Insane Tech | – | Build (provided) | Already available |
| KYC/ID verification | – | Smile ID, Youverify, or Prembly | Buy | $0.50–$1.00 per verification; not core competency |
| SMS/WhatsApp notifications | – | Twilio, Termii | Buy | Pay as you go; reliable |
| Payment/escrow (Phase 2\) | – | Paystack, Flutterwave, or licensed PSP | Buy | Avoid building payment rails |
| Hosting | – | AWS, Railway, or Supabase | Buy | Use free tier \+ credits |
| Database | – | Supabase (PostgreSQL) | Buy | Free tier for MVP |
| Monitoring | – | Sentry, LogRocket | Buy | Free tier for MVP |

### 18.6 Data Model (Core Entities – Simplified)

#### 18.6.1 User

| Field | Type | Description |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| `user_id` | UUID | Primary key |
| `phone_number` | String | Unique, used for login |
| `email` | String (optional) | Optional |
| `role` | Enum | broker, bdc, regulator, admin |
| `compliance_rung` | Integer (1-5) | Current compliance ladder level |
| `verification_status` | Enum | pending, verified, rejected |
| `bdc_license_number` | String | If BDC |
| `partner_bdc_id` | UUID | If broker partnered with BDC (Rung 4\) |
| `created_at` | Timestamp |  |
| `last_active_at` | Timestamp |  |

#### 18.6.2 Customer (Broker's Customer)

| Field | Type | Description |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| `customer_id` | UUID | Primary key |
| `broker_user_id` | UUID | FK to User (broker) |
| `name` | String | Customer name |
| `phone_number` | String |  |
| `id_type` | String | e.g., "NIN", "Passport", "Driver License" (for BDC KYC) |
| `id_number` | String (hashed) |  |
| `notes` | Text | Broker private notes |
| `total_volume` | Decimal | Lifetime volume with this broker |
| `last_transaction_at` | Timestamp |  |

#### 18.6.3 Trade Request

| Field | Type | Description |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| `trade_id` | UUID | Primary key |
| `type` | Enum | buy, sell |
| `currency` | String | USD, GBP, EUR |
| `amount` | Decimal |  |
| `customer_name` | String | Optional |
| `purpose_code` | String | CBN purpose codes (e.g., "P01" for school fees) |
| `broker_user_id` | UUID | FK to User (broker) |
| `bdc_user_id` | UUID | FK to User (BDC) – counterparty |
| `status` | Enum | pending, accepted, completed, failed, cancelled |
| `rate` | Decimal | Agreed exchange rate |
| `total_ngn` | Decimal | Amount \* rate |
| `escrow_status` | Enum | not\_used, held, released, refunded |
| `created_at` | Timestamp |  |
| `completed_at` | Timestamp |  |

#### 18.6.4 BDC Inventory

| Field | Type | Description |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| `inventory_id` | UUID | Primary key |
| `bdc_user_id` | UUID | FK to User (BDC) |
| `currency` | String | USD, GBP, EUR |
| `amount` | Decimal | Available amount |
| `rate` | Decimal | Selling rate |
| `is_visible_to_brokers` | Boolean | Whether shown in broker feed |
| `expires_at` | Timestamp | Rate validity |
| `updated_at` | Timestamp |  |

#### 18.6.5 Audit Log

| Field | Type | Description |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| `log_id` | UUID | Primary key |
| `user_id` | UUID | FK to User |
| `action_type` | String | trade\_request, login, quote\_generated, etc. |
| `action_details` | JSON | Variable payload |
| `ip_address_hash` | String | Hashed for privacy |
| `timestamp` | Timestamp |  |
| `immutable` | Boolean | Always true |

### 18.7 API Design (MVP – Internal and Future External)

**Internal APIs (for frontend):**

| Endpoint | Method | Purpose |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| `/auth/login` | POST | Phone number OTP |
| `/auth/verify` | POST | Verify OTP, create session |
| `/users/me` | GET | Current user profile |
| `/users/verify` | POST | Upload ID, selfie (Rung 3\) |
| `/trades/request` | POST | Create trade request (chat-to-trade) |
| `/trades` | GET | List user's trades |
| `/trades/{id}/accept` | POST | BDC accepts trade |
| `/trades/{id}/complete` | POST | Mark trade complete |
| `/quotes/generate` | POST | Generate rate quote |
| `/customers` | GET/POST | Manage customer list |
| `/inventory` | GET | BDCs: view own inventory |
| `/inventory/update` | POST | BDCs: update inventory |

**Future external APIs (Phase 3 for fintechs):**

| Endpoint | Method | Purpose |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| `/v1/rates` | GET | Real-time rates from BDCs |
| `/v1/quote` | POST | Request quote for specific amount |
| `/v1/trade` | POST | Execute trade (requires pre-approved BDC) |
| `/v1/trade/{id}/status` | GET | Check trade status |
| `/v1/webhooks` | POST | Settlement confirmations |

### 18.8 Security Architecture

| Control | Implementation |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Authentication** | JWT with short expiry (15 min) \+ refresh token |
| **OTP delivery** | SMS/WhatsApp via Twilio (rate-limited) |
| **Password policy** | No password (phone \+ OTP) – simpler for users |
| **API rate limiting** | 100 requests per minute per IP (adjustable) |
| **Input validation** | All user inputs validated and sanitized |
| **SQL injection prevention** | Parameterized queries (ORM) |
| **XSS prevention** | Output encoding, CSP headers |
| **CSRF protection** | SameSite cookies, anti-CSRF tokens for state-changing requests |
| **Encryption in transit** | TLS 1.3 (HTTPS) |
| **Encryption at rest** | AES-256 for sensitive fields (ID numbers, etc.) |
| **Sensitive data** | ID numbers hashed (not stored plaintext); KYC documents in S3 with signed URLs |
| **Audit logging** | All actions logged; logs immutable |
| **Session management** | User can view/logout other sessions |

### 18.9 Mobile UX – WhatsApp-Style Design

**Key design decisions to reduce broker learning curve:**

| Feature | WhatsApp Pattern | Cuboid Implementation |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Navigation | Bottom tabs | Chats, Customers, Quotes, Profile |
| Chat interface | Message bubbles | Trade requests appear as messages |
| Quick actions | Attach, emoji, voice | Quick rate request, customer selection |
| Notifications | Push for new messages | Push for trade updates, BDC responses |
| Search | Search chats, contacts | Search customers, past trades |
| Profile | Profile photo, status | Verification status, trust score |

**Broker home screen (mockup description):**

┌─────────────────────────────────────────┐

│  Cuboid                          ≡      │

├─────────────────────────────────────────┤

│  \[ Chat \] \[ Customers \] \[ Quotes \] \[Me\] │

├─────────────────────────────────────────┤

│  🔍 Search customers or trades...       │

├─────────────────────────────────────────┤

│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────┐│

│  │ 📱 Need $5k USD for school fees    ││

│  │    Today 10:32 AM                   ││

│  │    3 BDCs available                 ││

│  │    ➡️ View offers                   ││

│  └─────────────────────────────────────┘│

│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────┐│

│  │ ✓ Mr. John – $2k USD completed     ││

│  │    Yesterday 3:15 PM                ││

│  │    Receipt sent                     ││

│  └─────────────────────────────────────┘│

│  ┌─────────────────────────────────────┐│

│  │ 🟢 BDC in Ikeja has $10k USD       ││

│  │    Rate: NGN 760                    ││

│  │    Tap to request                   ││

│  └─────────────────────────────────────┘│

├─────────────────────────────────────────┤

│  \[ Type a message or FX request...   \] ▶│

└─────────────────────────────────────────┘

### 18.10 Development Roadmap (Technical)

| Phase | Duration | Focus | Key Deliverables |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **MVP Sprint 1** | Weeks 1-2 | Setup \+ auth | Insane Technologies integration, user registration, OTP |
| **MVP Sprint 2** | Weeks 3-4 | Chat-to-trade | Chat interface, trade request creation, BDC matching (manual) |
| **MVP Sprint 3** | Weeks 5-6 | Customer mgmt \+ quotes | Customer CRUD, quote generation, sharing |
| **MVP Sprint 4** | Weeks 7-8 | BDC features | Inventory management, trade acceptance, basic receipts |
| **MVP Sprint 5** | Weeks 9-10 | Escrow \+ settlement | Light escrow (manual confirmation), settlement tracking |
| **MVP Sprint 6** | Weeks 11-12 | Testing \+ launch | Bug fixes, performance, soft launch with pilot users |
| **Phase 2 (Sprints 7-12)** | Weeks 13-24 | Compliance \+ expansion | Automated filing, regulator dashboard, inter-BDC trading, Kano/Abuja launch |

### 18.11 Hosting and Infrastructure Cost Breakdown

| Service | Provider | MVP Monthly Cost | Notes |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Compute (backend) | AWS Lambda or Railway | $0 – $20 | Free tier initially |
| Database | Supabase (PostgreSQL) | $0 – $25 | Free tier includes 500MB |
| Object storage | AWS S3 | $0 – $5 | Minimal for MVP |
| CDN | Cloudflare | $0 | Free tier |
| SMS/WhatsApp | Twilio | $10 – $50 | OTPs, notifications |
| KYC verification | Smile ID | $20 – $100 | Based on volume |
| Monitoring | Sentry | $0 | Free tier |
| Domain \+ SSL | Namecheap \+ Let's Encrypt | $15/year | Negligible monthly |
| **Total monthly** |  | **$45 – $215** |  |

**Total hosting cost for first 12 months:** $540 – $2,580. Covered by $5,500 funding plus AWS/startup credits.

### 18.12 Scalability Considerations

| Component | MVP Capacity | Scaling Path |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Database (PostgreSQL) | 1,000 concurrent users | Read replicas, connection pooling |
| Chat (WebSockets) | 200 concurrent connections | Horizontal scaling (Redis pub/sub) |
| API (Express) | 500 req/sec | Load balancer, auto-scaling |
| Background jobs | Not implemented | Bull \+ Redis (Phase 2\) |

**Scaling trigger:** When daily active users exceed 500, implement Phase 2 scaling improvements.

### 18.13 Technical Risks and Mitigations

| Risk | Mitigation | Owner |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Insane Technologies modules have bugs | Shared QA; fallback to open-source if critical | Development |
| Chat infrastructure cannot scale | Use managed WebSocket service (e.g., Pusher) if needed | Development |
| SMS delivery fails (network issues) | Fallback to WhatsApp; retry logic | Development |
| Database performance degrades | Index optimization; read replicas | Development |
| Security breach | Regular audits; penetration testing (Phase 2\) | Development \+ Compliance |
| Third-party API downtime (Smile ID, Twilio) | Circuit breakers; fallback to manual verification | Development |

### 18.14 Summary: Technical Architecture

| Element | Summary |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Core principle** | Mobile-first, WhatsApp-style UX |
| **Foundation** | Insane Technologies provides auth, chat, ledger, API scaffolding ($25k–$45k value) |
| **Build vs buy** | Buy KYC, SMS, hosting; build trade, escrow, compliance |
| **Data model** | 5 core entities: User, Customer, Trade Request, BDC Inventory, Audit Log |
| **Security** | OTP auth, TLS, AES-256, immutable audit logs |
| **Hosting cost (MVP)** | $45 – $215/month (covered by $5,500) |
| **MVP timeline** | 12 weeks (Sprints 1-6) |
| **Scalability** | 1,000+ concurrent users before Phase 2 upgrades needed |

Here are **Section 19** and **Section 20** of the Cuboid Business Concept Note, continuing from where we left off. Formatted for Google Docs copy-paste.

## SECTION 19: OPERATIONS PLAN

### 19.1 Overview: Lean Operations for a Lean Platform

Cuboid's operations are designed to match its funding model—extremely lean, with manual processes replacing automation until volume justifies automation. The operations plan covers how Cuboid will onboard users, support them, handle settlements, manage compliance, and scale as volume grows.

**Operating principles:**

| Principle | Description |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Manual first, automate later** | Do things manually until the process is proven and volume justifies automation. |
| **Founder-led support** | Founders handle support initially to understand user pain points directly. |
| **Self-serve where possible** | Onboarding, documentation, FAQs reduce support load. |
| **Outsource non-core** | Legal, compliance consulting, KYC verification outsourced to specialists. |
| **Track everything** | Metrics drive decisions on when to automate or hire. |

### 19.2 Operational Phases

| Phase | Timing | Operations Model | Team Size (Ops) | Monthly Ops Cost |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **Phase 0: MVP Pilot** | Months 0-3 | Founder-led, manual everything | 1 (founder) | $0 – $200 |
| **Phase 1: Soft Launch** | Months 3-6 | Founder \+ part-time support | 1.5 | $200 – $500 |
| **Phase 2: Expansion** | Months 6-9 | Dedicated ops hire (part-time) | 2 | $500 – $1,000 |
| **Phase 3: Scale** | Months 9-12 | Full-time ops \+ part-time compliance | 2-3 | $1,000 – $2,500 |
| **Phase 4: Growth** | Months 12-18 | Ops team (3-4), compliance hire | 4-5 | $3,000 – $6,000 |

**Note:** All costs exclude founder salaries (sweat equity). Phase 4 costs assume seed funding.

### 19.3 User Onboarding Operations

#### 19.3.1 Broker Onboarding Workflow

| Step | Action | Owner | Time | Automation Level |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | Broker visits website, enters phone number | Self-serve | 1 min | Fully automated |
| 2 | System sends OTP via SMS/WhatsApp | Automated | 30 sec | Fully automated |
| 3 | Broker enters OTP, accepts terms | Self-serve | 1 min | Fully automated |
| 4 | Account created (Rung 2\) | Automated | Instant | Fully automated |
| 5 | (Optional) Broker upgrades to Rung 3 by uploading ID | Self-serve \+ third-party KYC | 3-5 min | Semi-automated |
| 6 | (Optional) Manual review if ID verification fails | Compliance (outsourced) | 1-2 hours | Manual |

**Broker onboarding target:** \<5 minutes from site visit to first trade request.

#### 19.3.2 BDC Onboarding Workflow

| Step | Action | Owner | Time | Automation Level |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | BDC expresses interest (form, call, referral) | Sales (founder) | 5 min | Manual |
| 2 | Sales sends demo video and pricing | Automated email | 1 min | Automated |
| 3 | BDC agrees to proceed | BDC | Varies | Manual |
| 4 | KYB verification: BDC uploads license, CAC, director IDs | Self-serve \+ compliance review | 1-2 days | Semi-automated |
| 5 | Compliance consultant verifies documents | Outsourced compliance | 2-4 hours | Manual |
| 6 | Account created, BDC configured (branches, users) | Ops (founder) | 30 min | Manual |
| 7 | Training call (15-30 min) | Sales/Support | 30 min | Manual |
| 8 | BDC makes first inventory entry or trade | BDC | Varies | Self-serve |

**BDC onboarding target:** 2-5 days from expression of interest to first trade.

#### 19.3.3 Kyc/Kyb Verification Process

| User Type | Verification Required | Method | Cost | Provider |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Broker (Rung 3\) | Government ID, selfie | Third-party API | $0.50 – $1.00 | Smile ID, Youverify, or Prembly |
| BDC (Rung 5\) | License, CAC, director IDs | Manual review \+ API check | $5 – $10 (manual) | Manual \+ NIBSS/CAC |
| Regulator | Official email domain | Automated | Free | N/A |

**Verification queue management:**

- Target response time: \<2 hours for BDC KYB, \<30 minutes for broker ID failures.  
- Escalation: If third-party API fails, manual review by compliance consultant.

### 19.4 Customer Support Operations

#### 19.4.1 Support Channels (Phased)

| Channel | Phase 0-1 (M0-6) | Phase 2-3 (M6-12) | Phase 4 (M12+) |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| In-app chat (support) | No (founder WhatsApp) | Yes (simple form) | Yes (ticketed) |
| Email support | [support@cuboid.com](mailto:support@cuboid.com) (founder) | [support@cuboid.com](mailto:support@cuboid.com) (dedicated) | support \+ Zendesk |
| Phone support | Founder's number (pilot only) | No (scales poorly) | No |
| FAQ/Knowledge base | Basic page | Expanded | Full documentation |
| WhatsApp broadcast | For broker updates | Automated | Automated |

#### 19.4.2 Support SLAs

| Issue Type | Phase 0-1 | Phase 2-3 | Phase 4 | Escalation |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Critical (cannot trade) | \<2 hours | \<1 hour | \<30 min | Founder |
| Major (feature broken) | \<1 day | \<4 hours | \<2 hours | Ops lead |
| Minor (question, guidance) | \<1 day | \<1 day | \<4 hours | Support |
| Feature request | Logged, reviewed weekly | Logged, reviewed weekly | Logged, triaged monthly | Product |

#### 19.4.3 Support Volume Estimates

| User Type | Phase 1 (50 users) | Phase 3 (500 users) | Phase 4 (2,000 users) |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Tickets per user per week | 0.5 | 0.3 | 0.2 |
| Total weekly tickets | 25 | 150 | 400 |
| Minutes per ticket | 5 | 5 | 3 |
| Weekly support hours | 2 | 12.5 | 20 |
| Support FTE equivalent | 0.05 | 0.3 | 0.5 |

**Conclusion:** Founder-led support is feasible until Phase 4 (2,000+ users). At that point, dedicated support hire is needed.

### 19.5 Settlement Operations

Settlement is the process of moving funds between parties (customer → broker → BDC or customer → BDC). Cuboid facilitates but does not execute settlement (to avoid licensing requirements).

#### 19.5.1 Settlement Flow (Broker-BDC Trade)

| Step | Action | Responsible | Tracking Method |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | Customer sends naira to broker (or escrow) | Customer | Broker confirms receipt in app |
| 2 | Broker sends naira to BDC | Broker | BDC confirms receipt in app |
| 3 | BDC sends USD to customer (or confirms delivery) | BDC | Customer confirms OR BDC uploads proof |
| 4 | (If escrow used) Escrow releases funds to broker | Escrow agent | System webhook |

**Manual settlement tracking (MVP):** Both parties confirm each step. System logs confirmation. Disputes handled manually by founder.

**Automated settlement tracking (Phase 2):** Integration with bank APIs (Paystack, Flutterwave) to confirm transfers automatically.

#### 19.5.2 Settlement Disputes

| Dispute Type | Resolution Process | Escalation |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Customer claims they paid, broker claims no | Request proof of transfer (screenshot, bank reference) | Founder reviews; if unresolved, suggest legal action |
| Broker claims they paid BDC, BDC claims no | Request proof of transfer; check BDC inventory | Founder reviews; BDC may be suspended |
| BDC claims they delivered USD, customer claims no | Request delivery proof (receipt, bank statement) | Founder reviews; BDC required to provide proof |
| Escrow funds disputed | Escrow agent follows agreement (24-hour hold, then release based on evidence) | Legal counsel |

**Target:** \<5% of trades disputed. \<1% unresolved after 48 hours.

### 19.6 Compliance Operations

#### 19.6.1 Daily Compliance Tasks (Phase 1-2)

| Task | Frequency | Owner | Time |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Review flagged suspicious activity | Daily | Compliance consultant (outsourced) | 15-30 min |
| Respond to regulator inquiries (if any) | As needed | Founder | Varies |
| Check KYC/KYB queue (failed verifications) | Daily | Compliance consultant | 15 min |
| Update compliance ladder nudges | Weekly | Product | 30 min |
| Review terms of service compliance | Monthly | Legal consultant | 1 hour |

#### 19.6.2 Suspicious Activity Review Process

┌─────────────────┐

│ System flags    │

│ suspicious      │

│ activity        │

└────────┬────────┘

         ▼

┌─────────────────┐

│ Automated rule: │

│ \>10 trades/hour │

│ \>$50k/week      │

│ Structuring     │

└────────┬────────┘

         ▼

┌─────────────────┐

│ Queue for       │

│ human review    │

└────────┬────────┘

         ▼

┌─────────────────┐

│ Compliance      │

│ reviews context │

│ (trade history, │

│ counterparties) │

└────────┬────────┘

         ▼

    ┌────┴────┐

    │ Flag    │ No flag

    │ valid?  │

    └────┬────┘

         ▼

┌─────────────────┐

│ Draft STR       │

│ Notify BDC      │

│ (if applicable) │

└────────┬────────┘

         ▼

┌─────────────────┐

│ BDC reviews/    │

│ submits to NFIU │

│ (or Cuboid      │

│ submits if BDC  │

│ fails to act)   │

└─────────────────┘

### 19.7 Partner Management Operations

#### 19.7.1 BDC Relationship Management

| Activity | Frequency | Owner | Notes |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Check-in call | Monthly (first 3 months), then quarterly | Sales/Founder | For BDCs \>$100k monthly volume |
| Product feedback collection | Monthly | Product | Via call or form |
| Compliance health check | Quarterly | Compliance | Filing status, flagged transactions |
| Renewal reminder | 30 days before subscription expiry | Automated | Email with payment link |
| At-risk intervention | When volume drops \>50% MoM | Sales | Call to understand issue |

#### 19.7.2 Broker Community Management

| Activity | Frequency | Owner | Notes |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| WhatsApp broadcast (tips, updates) | Weekly | Marketing | Opt-in only |
| Referral program updates | Monthly | Ops | Earnings statements |
| Compliance ladder nudges | Automatic | System | Based on volume thresholds |
| Top broker recognition | Monthly | Marketing | "Broker of the Month" – badge, small incentive |

#### 19.7.3 Regulator Relationship Management

| Activity | Frequency | Owner | Notes |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Sandbox progress update | Monthly | Founder | Email to CBN contact |
| Data share (anonymized) | Monthly (Phase 2+) | Compliance | Aggregated volume, trends |
| Dashboard demo | Quarterly (Phase 2+) | Product | Show new features |
| Formal meeting | Bi-annually | Founder | In-person or virtual |

### 19.8 Operations Metrics Dashboard

| Metric | Phase 1 Target | Phase 3 Target | How to Measure |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| User onboarding time (broker) | \<5 min | \<3 min | Analytics |
| User onboarding time (BDC) | \<5 days | \<2 days | CRM tracking |
| Support response time (critical) | \<2 hours | \<30 min | Support ticket system |
| Support resolution rate (24h) | 80% | 95% | Support ticket system |
| Settlement dispute rate | \<10% | \<5% | Trade data |
| Settlement dispute resolution time | \<48 hours | \<24 hours | Manual tracking |
| Compliance flag review time | \<4 hours | \<2 hours | Queue tracking |
| BDC churn rate (monthly) | \<5% | \<3% | Subscription data |
| Broker churn rate (monthly) | \<10% | \<7% | Activity data |
| Uptime (service availability) | 99% | 99.5% | Monitoring |

### 19.9 Operational Risk Register

| Risk | Likelihood | Impact | Mitigation | Owner |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Founder burnout (single point of failure) | Medium | High | Document processes; train backup; phase 4 hires | Founder |
| Settlement dispute escalates to legal | Low | Medium | Clear terms; escrow for high-value trades | Legal |
| BDC churn due to poor support | Medium | Medium | Dedicated BDC contact; proactive check-ins | Sales |
| Broker churn due to complexity | Medium | Medium | Simplify UX; video tutorials; WhatsApp support | Product |
| Compliance consultant unavailable | Low | Medium | Multiple consultants on retainer | Founder |
| Regulator requests data with short notice | Low | High | Audit logs accessible; dashboard ready | Compliance |

### 19.10 Operational Cost Breakdown (Monthly, by Phase)

| Cost Category | Phase 0-1 (M0-6) | Phase 2-3 (M6-12) | Phase 4 (M12-18) |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Hosting & infrastructure | $50 – $150 | $150 – $400 | $400 – $1,000 |
| Third-party APIs (KYC, SMS) | $50 – $150 | $150 – $500 | $500 – $2,000 |
| Compliance consultant (outsourced) | $200 – $500 | $500 – $1,000 | $1,000 – $2,000 |
| Legal (retainer) | $100 – $200 | $200 – $500 | $500 – $1,000 |
| Sales & marketing (minimal) | $50 – $100 | $100 – $500 | $500 – $2,000 |
| Part-time ops support | $0 | $0 – $500 | $1,000 – $2,000 |
| Full-time compliance | $0 | $0 | $1,500 – $2,500 |
| **Total monthly ops cost** | **$450 – $1,100** | **$1,100 – $3,400** | **$5,400 – $12,500** |

**Note:** Phase 4 costs assume seed funding ($50k–$100k). Phases 0-3 are covered by the initial $5,500 strategic round.

### 19.11 Summary: Operations Plan

| Element | Summary |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Operating model** | Manual first, automate later. Founder-led support. |
| **Broker onboarding** | \<5 minutes, fully automated (ID verification optional). |
| **BDC onboarding** | 2-5 days, semi-automated with manual KYB review. |
| **Settlement** | Manual confirmation initially; API integration in Phase 2\. |
| **Compliance** | Outsourced consultant \+ automated flagging. |
| **Support** | Founder-led until 2,000+ users. |
| **Cost (Phase 0-3)** | $450 – $1,100/month – covered by $5,500. |
| **Cost (Phase 4\)** | $5,400 – $12,500/month – requires seed funding. |

## SECTION 20: DEVELOPMENT ROADMAP – LEAN, $5,500

### 20.1 Overview: Building Only What Matters

With only $5,500 in initial funding, Cuboid cannot afford to build features that users do not need. The development roadmap is ruthlessly prioritized around **broker adoption** and **BDC participation**.

**Roadmap principles:**

| Principle | Application |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Broker features first** | Chat-to-trade, quotes, customer management – these drive volume. |
| **BDC features second** | Inventory management, receipts, inter-BDC trading – these enable compliance and revenue. |
| **Compliance features third** | Automated filing, regulator dashboard – these come after volume proves value. |
| **API last** | Fintech integration only after platform is stable and has volume. |
| **Manual processes over automation** | Do manually until volume justifies automation cost. |

### 20.2 Development Sprints Overview (12 Weeks to MVP)

| Sprint | Weeks | Focus | Key Deliverables | Budget Allocation |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **Sprint 0** | Week 0-1 | Setup & foundation | Environment, auth, user registration | $300 |
| **Sprint 1** | Week 1-3 | Broker core features | Chat-to-trade (basic), quote generator | $800 |
| **Sprint 2** | Week 3-5 | Broker retention | Customer management, trade history | $800 |
| **Sprint 3** | Week 5-7 | BDC core features | Inventory management, trade acceptance, receipts | $800 |
| **Sprint 4** | Week 7-9 | Matching & escrow | BDC inventory feed for brokers, light escrow (manual) | $600 |
| **Sprint 5** | Week 9-10 | Compliance basics | Audit logging, compliance ladder (Rungs 1-3) | $300 |
| **Sprint 6** | Week 10-12 | Testing & polish | Bug fixes, performance, documentation | $300 |

**Total development budget:** $3,900 (70% of $5,500). Remaining $1,600 allocated to hosting, legal, and broker outreach.

### 20.3 Sprint 0: Setup & Foundation (Week 0-1)

| Task | Description | Owner | Hours |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Environment setup | AWS/Railway account, Supabase database | Dev | 5 |
| Insane Technologies integration | Auth, chat engine, ledger modules | Dev | 10 |
| User registration | Phone number \+ OTP (Twilio) | Dev | 8 |
| Role selection | Broker vs BDC vs regulator (basic) | Dev | 4 |
| Basic UI framework | Mobile-first React app skeleton | Dev | 8 |
| **Total** |  |  | **35 hours** |

**Success criteria:** User can register, receive OTP, login, see dashboard.

### 20.4 Sprint 1: Broker Core Features (Week 1-3)

| Task | Description | Owner | Hours |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Chat interface | WhatsApp-style chat UI | Dev | 12 |
| Chat-to-trade NLP | Parse "need $5k USD" – extract amount, currency | Dev | 10 |
| BDC inventory stub | Hardcoded BDC inventory for MVP | Dev | 4 |
| Quote generator | Generate rate quote based on inventory | Dev | 8 |
| Quote sharing | Copy to clipboard, share via WhatsApp | Dev | 4 |
| Trade request creation | Send request to selected BDC | Dev | 8 |
| **Total** |  |  | **46 hours** |

**Success criteria:** Broker can type "need $5k USD", see BDC options, generate quote, send trade request.

### 20.8 Sprint 5: Compliance Basics (Week 9-10)

### 20.10 Post-MVP Roadmap (Months 3-12)

| Sprint Group | Weeks | Focus | Key Deliverables |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **Sprint 7-8** | 12-16 | Phase 2: Kano launch | Multi-city support, localization, broker recruitment tools |
| **Sprint 9-10** | 16-20 | Phase 2: Compliance automation | One-click CBN filing, goAML export |
| **Sprint 11-12** | 20-24 | Phase 2: Inter-BDC trading | Automated matching, settlement netting |
| **Sprint 13-14** | 24-28 | Phase 2: Regulator dashboard | Read-only dashboard for CBN/NFIU |
| **Sprint 15-16** | 28-32 | Phase 2: Abuja launch | Geographic expansion |
| **Sprint 17-20** | 32-40 | Phase 3: API for fintechs | External API, documentation, pilot partners |
| **Sprint 21-24** | 40-48 | Phase 3: National scale | Port Harcourt, Ibadan, other cities |

### 20.11 Development Team (Lean)

| Role | Phase 0-1 (M0-6) | Phase 2 (M6-12) | Phase 3 (M12-18) | Hourly Rate |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Lead developer (contractor) | 20-30 hours/week | 30-40 hours/week | 40 hours/week (full-time) | $20 – $30 |
| Junior/QA (contractor) | 0 | 10-20 hours/week | 20-30 hours/week | $10 – $15 |
| Insane Technologies (strategic) | Technical advisory (free) | Technical advisory (free) | Technical advisory (free) | $0 (equity) |
| Founder (product/ops) | Full-time (sweat equity) | Full-time (sweat equity) | Full-time (sweat equity) | $0 |

**Total development cost (Phase 0-1, 6 months):**

- Lead dev: 25h/week × 24 weeks × $25 \= $15,000 (estimated)  
- But note: This exceeds $5,500 budget significantly.

**Correction:** The $5,500 funding covers only **initial MVP development (Sprints 0-6, 12 weeks)** at approximately $25/hour × 300 hours \= $7,500? This still exceeds $5,500.

**Reconciliation:** The $5,500 strategic round is supplemented by **sweat equity from founder** (who codes or manages contractors with extreme efficiency) and **Insane Technologies contributed modules** that reduce development time from \~500 hours to \~250 hours.

**Adjusted calculation:**

| Resource | Hours | Rate | Cost | Source |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Lead developer (contractor) | 150 | $20 | $3,000 | $5,500 funding |
| Founder (sweat equity) | 100 | $0 | $0 | Founder |
| Insane Technologies (provided modules) | \~200 hours saved | $0 | $0 | 25% equity |
| **Total effective development** | **450 hours** | **$3,000 cash** | **$3,000** |  |

**Total cash from $5,500:** $3,000 to development \+ $2,500 to legal, hosting, outreach.

### 20.12 Development Metrics and Success Criteria

### 20.13 Technical Debt and Future Investment Needs

| Area | MVP Approach | Technical Debt | Future Investment (Seed Round) |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Settlement | Manual confirmation | High (manual processes) | Bank API integration ($2k – $5k) |
| Escrow | Manual tracking | Medium | Licensed escrow provider integration ($3k – $8k) |

## SECTION 21: REVENUE MODEL & PRICING

### 21.1 Overview: Five Revenue Streams, One Platform

Cuboid generates revenue through five primary streams, each tied to a specific user segment and value proposition. The model is designed to **capture value from volume** (transaction fees) while building **stable recurring revenue** (subscriptions).

**Revenue streams summary:**

| Stream | Primary User | Model | Expected Share (Year 2\) |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Transaction fees (broker-BDC trades) | Brokers, BDCs | 0.1% – 0.3% of trade value | 40% |
| BDC Management Module subscription | Licensed BDCs | $20 – $100 per month | 30% |
| Compliance-as-a-Service (add-on) | Licensed BDCs | $10 – $30 per month | 10% |
| Inter-BDC trading spread | Licensed BDCs | 0.05% – 0.1% of trade value | 10% |
| API access (fintechs, banks) | Fintechs, PSPs, banks | $500 – $2,000 per month \+ transaction fees | 10% |

**Year 2 revenue mix (moderate adoption scenario):**

Total Annual Revenue: $500,000 (moderate)

Transaction fees (broker-BDC)    $200,000 (40%)  ████████████████████

BDC Subscription                  $150,000 (30%)  ███████████████

Compliance add-on                  $50,000 (10%)  █████

Inter-BDC spread                   $50,000 (10%)  █████

API access                         $50,000 (10%)  █████

### 21.2 Stream 1: Transaction Fees (Broker-BDC Trades)

**Description:** Cuboid charges a small percentage of each trade executed between a broker and a licensed BDC.

**Rationale:** Brokers and BDCs currently pay no platform fees (they trade via WhatsApp/phone). Cuboid must keep fees low enough to be negligible compared to their spread, but high enough to generate revenue.

**Fee structure (tiered by volume):**

| Monthly Volume (per BDC or per broker) | Fee Rate | Effective Cost per $10k Trade |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| \< $100,000 | 0.3% | $30 |
| $100,000 – $500,000 | 0.25% | $25 |
| $500,000 – $1,000,000 | 0.2% | $20 |
| \> $1,000,000 | 0.15% | $15 |

**Who pays:** The fee can be split between broker and BDC, or paid by one party. Default: 0.15% from broker, 0.15% from BDC (total 0.3%). Parties can negotiate.

**Example:** Broker trades $50,000 with BDC in a month. Fee \= 0.3% × $50,000 \= $150. Split: broker pays $75, BDC pays $75.

**Revenue projection:**

| Year | Total Broker-BDC Volume (SOM) | Average Fee Rate | Transaction Fee Revenue |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | $4M – $8M | 0.25% | $10,000 – $20,000 |
| 2 | $75M – $150M | 0.2% | $150,000 – $300,000 |
| 3 | $300M – $600M | 0.15% – 0.2% | $450,000 – $1,200,000 |

### 21.3 Stream 2: BDC Management Module Subscription

**Description:** Monthly SaaS fee for licensed BDCs to access inventory management, customer management, digital receipts, inter-BDC trading, and broker demand feed.

**Pricing tiers:**

| Tier | Monthly Price | Features | Target BDC |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **Lite** | $20 | Inventory (basic), customer mgmt (100 customers), digital receipts, basic reports | Small BDC (\<$500k monthly volume) |
| **Pro** | $50 | Lite \+ inter-BDC trading, broker demand feed, 500 customers, transaction export, priority support | Medium BDC ($500k–$2M monthly volume) |
| **Enterprise** | $100 | Pro \+ multi-branch (3 branches included), compliance automation (add-on available), dedicated account manager | Large BDC (\>$2M monthly volume) |

**Volume discounts:**

- 10% off for annual prepayment  
- Additional 10% off for BDCs with \>$1M monthly volume on platform (combined discount up to 20%)

**Revenue projection:**

| Year | BDCs on Platform (avg) | Average Subscription | Annual Subscription Revenue |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | 25 | $35 | $10,500 |
| 2 | 150 | $45 | $81,000 |
| 3 | 400 | $55 | $264,000 |

**Note:** Year 3 assumes higher Enterprise adoption as BDC volume grows.

### 21.4 Stream 3: Compliance-as-a-Service (Add-On)

**Description:** Optional add-on for BDCs that automates CBN/NFIU filing. BDCs currently spend 10–20 hours per week on compliance; this feature saves them time and avoids fines.

**Pricing:**

| Feature | Monthly Price | Included in Which Tier? |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Automated CBN daily returns | $10 | Add-on for Lite/Pro; included in Enterprise |
| Automated weekly positions | $5 | Add-on for Lite/Pro; included in Enterprise |
| CTR/STR generation (goAML format) | $10 | Add-on for Lite/Pro; included in Enterprise |
| One-click filing (or API push) | $5 | Add-on for all tiers |
| **Full compliance bundle** | **$25** ($20 for Pro, $15 for Enterprise) |  |

**Full compliance bundle pricing by tier:**

| BDC Tier | Monthly Add-on Price | Total Monthly (Subscription \+ Compliance) |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Lite | $25 | $45 |
| Pro | $20 | $70 |
| Enterprise | $15 (or included) | $115 (or $100 if included) |

**Revenue projection:**

| Year | BDCs Using Compliance Add-on | Average Add-on Price | Annual Add-on Revenue |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | 10 (40% of BDCs) | $20 | $2,400 |
| 2 | 90 (60% of BDCs) | $22 | $23,760 |
| 3 | 300 (75% of BDCs) | $24 | $86,400 |

### 21.5 Stream 4: Inter-BDC Trading Spread

**Description:** Cuboid captures a small spread on trades between licensed BDCs. This is separate from the broker-BDC transaction fee.

**How it works:**

| Scenario | BDC A (Excess) | BDC B (Deficit) | Cuboid |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| BDC A offers USD at | NGN 760 |  |  |
| BDC B sees offer |  | Wants to buy at NGN 760 |  |
| Cuboid matches | Sells at NGN 759.50 | Buys at NGN 760.50 | Spread: NGN 1.00 |
| Effective spread | 0.065% | 0.065% | 0.13% total |

**Spread range:** 0.05% – 0.1% per side (0.1% – 0.2% total).

**Who pays:** Both BDCs effectively pay half the spread. The spread is embedded in the rate (no separate fee).

**Revenue projection:**

| Year | Inter-BDC Volume (SOM) | Average Spread | Spread Revenue |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | $500k – $1M | 0.1% | $500 – $1,000 |
| 2 | $10M – $25M | 0.08% | $8,000 – $20,000 |
| 3 | $50M – $150M | 0.06% | $30,000 – $90,000 |

### 21.6 Stream 5: API Access (Fintechs, Banks, PSPs)

**Description:** Third-party platforms (fintechs, banks, payment service providers) pay to integrate Cuboid's BDC network into their own applications.

**Pricing tiers (per month):**

| Tier | Monthly Fee | Transaction Fee (additional) | Volume Limit | Features |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **Developer** | $0 | 0.5% | 100 API calls/day | Sandbox only, test environment |
| **Startup** | $500 | 0.3% | 10,000 calls/month | Live API, basic support |
| **Business** | $1,000 | 0.25% | 100,000 calls/month | Live API, priority support, SLA |
| **Enterprise** | $2,000+ | Negotiated (0.15% – 0.2%) | Custom | Dedicated support, custom integration |

**What the API provides:**

| Endpoint | Description |
| :---- | :---- |
| `GET /rates` | Real-time rates from BDCs on platform |
| `POST /quote` | Request a quote for a specific amount |
| `POST /trade` | Execute a trade (requires pre-approved BDC partner) |
| `GET /trade/{id}/status` | Check trade status |
| `POST /webhooks` | Settlement confirmations |

**Target API customers:**

- Fintechs (e.g., Paystack, Flutterwave, Moniepoint, OPay) – want to offer FX to their merchants  
- Banks (e.g., GTBank, Access, UBA) – want to offer retail FX without building their own BDC network  
- PSPs (e.g., Nomba, TeamApt) – cross-border payment facilitators

**Revenue projection:**

| Year | API Partners | Average Monthly Fee | Annual API Revenue |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | 0 (Phase 3\) | – | $0 |
| 2 | 3 | $800 | $28,800 |
| 3 | 10 | $1,000 | $120,000 |

### 21.7 Pricing Philosophy and Justification

| Principle | Explanation | Example |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **Low entry barrier** | Brokers pay nothing upfront; fees come from transaction volume. BDCs pay low monthly subscription ($20–$100). | Broker: $0/month \+ 0.3% of trades. |
| **Volume discounts** | Higher volume \= lower effective fee. Aligns incentives. | BDC trading $1M/month pays 0.15% instead of 0.3%. |
| **Value-based, not cost-based** | Fees are a small fraction of value delivered. Cuboid saves BDCs $10k+ per year; charging $600/year is reasonable. | ROI calculation in Section 12.5. |
| **Transparent** | No hidden fees. Brokers and BDCs see exactly what they pay. | Fee displayed before trade confirmation. |
| **No lock-in** | No long-term contracts. Month-to-month subscription. | BDC can cancel anytime (but loses network benefits). |

### 21.8 Comparison to Alternatives

| Alternative | Cost to BDC/Broker | Value Provided | Cuboid Advantage |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Excel/paper (status quo) | $0 (but labor \~$10k/year) | None | Cuboid saves labor, reduces fines |
| Custom software (e.g., Finacle) | $5,000+ upfront \+ $500/month | Inventory, receipts | Cuboid is 1/10th cost \+ network effects |
| Bank-provided portal | $0 (but bank-specific) | Limited reporting | Cuboid is BDC-owned, not bank-dependent |
| WhatsApp trading (brokers) | $0 | Communication only | Cuboid adds inventory visibility, escrow, customer mgmt |
| Cuboid | $20–$100/month \+ 0.15–0.3% | All of above \+ network | Only platform with both broker appeal and compliance |

## SECTION 22: FUNDING REQUIREMENTS – $5,500 MINIMUM – STRATEGIC ROUND

### 22.1 Overview: The Most Aggressively Lean Fintech Round

Cuboid is seeking a **minimum of $5,500** in strategic funding. This is not a typical seed round. It is an **overly discounted strategic round** designed for hands-on partners who bring more than money—network access, development capacity, or regulatory relationships.

**Why so low?** Cuboid is built on Insane Technologies' existing infrastructure (valued at $25,000 – $45,000, contributed in exchange for 25% equity). The $5,500 covers only cash expenses: hosting, legal, third-party APIs, and minimal contract development. Founder labor is sweat equity.

**The strategic rationale:** A larger round ($50k+) would require a higher valuation, more dilution, and more time to raise. Cuboid does not need cash to build—it needs cash to **operate** while building. The $5,500 round can close in days, not months.

### 22.2 Use of Funds (Detailed)

| Category | Item | Estimated Cost | Notes |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **Development** | Contract developer (150 hours @ $20/hr) | $3,000 | MVP development (Sprints 0-6) |
| **Hosting & infrastructure** | AWS/Supabase/Twilio credits (12 months) | $800 | Free tier \+ startup credits reduce cost |
| **Legal** | Entity registration (CAC) | $160 |  |
| **Legal** | Legal opinion (licensing) | $1,000 – $1,500 | Nigerian fintech law firm |
| **Legal** | Terms of service, agreements | $400 | Templates \+ customization |
| **Legal** | Shareholders' agreement | $500 – $800 | Founders \+ Insane Technologies |
| **KYC/Verification** | Smile ID credits (500 verifications) | $250 | $0.50 per verification |
| **Outreach** | Broker recruitment (WhatsApp, airtime) | $300 | Pilot broker incentives |
| **Outreach** | BDC outreach (flyers, visits) | $200 | Lagos pilot |
| **Contingency** | Unexpected expenses | $390 – $890 | 10-20% buffer |
| **Total** |  | **$5,500** |  |

**Note:** The $5,500 is a **minimum**. Up to $20,000 may be accepted in this strategic round, with additional funds allocated to extended development, marketing, and contingency.

### 22.3 Funding Timeline and Milestones

| Month | Milestone | Cumulative Spend | Remaining |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 0 (Funding close) | $5,500 raised | $0 | $5,500 |
| 1 | Entity registration, legal agreements | $1,500 | $4,000 |
| 2 | MVP Sprint 0-3 (development) | $2,500 | $1,500 |
| 3 | MVP Sprint 4-6 (development complete) | $4,000 | $1,500 |
| 4 | MVP launch (pilot brokers \+ BDCs) | $4,500 | $1,000 |
| 5 | Phase 2 development begins | $5,000 | $500 |
| 6 | Hosting, KYC credits renew | $5,500 | $0 |

**At Month 6, Cuboid will have:** Live MVP, 20–50 brokers, 5–10 BDCs, positive volume, and early revenue. This track record enables a formal seed round ($50k–$100k).

### 22.4 Equity Offered (Strategic Round)

| Investment Amount | Equity Range (Founder Pool) | Investor Rights | Notes |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| $5,500 (minimum) | 5% – 10% | Information rights (quarterly updates) | Single investor or syndicate |
| $10,000 | 10% – 15% | Information rights \+ right to attend board as observer |  |
| $20,000 (maximum) | 15% – 20% | Information rights \+ board observer \+ pro-rata in future rounds |  |

**Important disclosures to investors:**

1. **Insane Technologies holds minimum 25% equity** and this round does not dilute them. The equity offered comes from the **founding team pool** (or is structured as a convertible note that converts into founder pool shares).  
     
2. **This is an overly discounted round.** The nominal pre-money valuation is $50,000 – $100,000, which is far below the value of Insane Technologies' contributed infrastructure ($25k–$45k) \+ founder sweat equity. Investors are receiving a significant discount in exchange for speed and hands-on support.  
     
3. **Future rounds will be at significantly higher valuations.** The seed round (Month 12-18) will target $500k – $1M pre-money. Strategic round investors who participate pro-rata will benefit from this appreciation.  
     
4. **No salaries for founders.** All founding team labor is sweat equity. The $5,500 covers only external expenses.

### 22.5 Investor Criteria (Who This Round Is For)

| Criterion | Description |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Hands-on** | Investor contributes more than money: network access (brokers, BDCs, banks), development capacity, or regulatory relationships. |
| **Patient** | Understands that Cuboid is building for long-term value, not quick exit. |
| **Broker/BDC network** | Has existing relationships with informal brokers or licensed BDCs in Lagos, Kano, or Abuja. |
| **Fintech experience** | Has built or invested in Nigerian fintech before; understands regulatory landscape. |
| **Small check** | Can write a check for $5,500 – $20,000 without extensive due diligence. |

**This round is NOT for:**

- Passive investors who only write checks.  
- Investors seeking immediate returns.  
- Investors uncomfortable with grey-market dynamics (brokers as primary movers).

### 22.6 Use of Funds – Detailed Justification

#### 22.6.1 Development ($3,000)

| Task | Hours | Rate | Cost |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Authentication & user registration (Insane Tech foundation) | 10 | $20 | $200 |
| Chat interface & chat-to-trade NLP | 25 | $20 | $500 |
| Quote generator | 15 | $20 | $300 |
| Customer management | 20 | $20 | $400 |
| BDC inventory management | 20 | $20 | $400 |
| Trade acceptance & receipts | 20 | $20 | $400 |
| Light escrow (manual) | 15 | $20 | $300 |
| Audit logging & compliance basics | 15 | $20 | $300 |
| Testing, bug fixes, polish | 10 | $20 | $200 |
| **Total** | **150 hours** |  | **$3,000** |

**Why contractor vs full-time:** A contractor allows flexible hours without overhead (benefits, office). $20/hour is competitive for Nigerian developers with 2-4 years experience.

#### 22.6.2 Legal ($2,060 – $2,860)

| Item | Estimated Cost | Vendor |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| CAC registration | $160 | Corporate affairs commission (self-file or agent) |
| Legal opinion (licensing) | $1,000 – $1,500 | Nigerian law firm (TLcom, Udo Udoma, or similar) |
| Terms of service (broker, BDC) | $300 – $500 | Legal template \+ lawyer customization |
| Shareholders' agreement | $500 – $800 | Lawyer (bundled with opinion) |

**Why legal opinion is critical:** To demonstrate to regulators and investors that Cuboid has sought and received legal advice confirming that its proposed activities do not require a BDC or banking license.

#### 22.6.3 Hosting & Infrastructure ($800)

| Item | Estimated 12-month Cost | Provider |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Compute (backend) | $0 – $100 (free tier \+ credits) | AWS, Railway, or Vercel |
| Database | $0 – $200 (free tier) | Supabase |
| SMS/WhatsApp (OTP, notifications) | $300 – $500 | Twilio or Termii |
| Object storage (receipts, documents) | $0 – $50 | AWS S3 or Cloudflare R2 |
| Domain \+ SSL | $15 | Namecheap \+ Let's Encrypt |
| Monitoring (Sentry, LogRocket) | $0 | Free tier |
| **Total** | **$315 – $865** |  |

**Assumption:** Startup credits (AWS Activate, etc.) reduce actual cash outlay. $800 budget is conservative.

#### 22.6.4 Outreach & Pilot Incentives ($500)

| Item | Cost | Purpose |
| :---- | :---- | :---- |
| WhatsApp broadcast credits | $100 | Reach broker groups |
| Airtime for pilot brokers | $200 | Incentive for early adopters (20 brokers × $10) |
| Flyers for BDC shops | $100 | Physical outreach in Lagos |
| BDC pilot incentives (coffee/transport) | $100 | Thank you for early BDCs |

### 22.7 Cash Flow Projection (First 12 Months)

| Month | Inflow | Outflow | Cumulative Balance |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 0 | $5,500 | $0 | $5,500 |
| 1 | $0 | $1,500 (legal, entity) | $4,000 |
| 2 | $0 | $1,000 (development) | $3,000 |
| 3 | $0 | $1,000 (development) | $2,000 |
| 4 | $200 (first revenue) | $500 (hosting, KYC) | $1,700 |
| 5 | $300 | $500 | $1,500 |
| 6 | $500 | $500 | $1,500 |
| 7 | $700 | $500 | $1,700 |
| 8 | $900 | $500 | $2,100 |
| 9 | $1,200 | $500 | $2,800 |
| 10 | $1,500 | $500 | $3,800 |
| 11 | $1,800 | $500 | $5,100 |
| 12 | $2,200 | $500 | $6,800 |

**At Month 12:** Positive cash flow ($6,800 balance), growing revenue, and a track record for seed round.

### 22.8 Return on Investment (For Strategic Round Investors)

**Assumptions:**

- Strategic round: $5,500 for 10% equity (example).  
- Seed round (Month 12): $100,000 at $800,000 pre-money valuation.  
- Series A (Month 24): $1M at $5M pre-money valuation.  
- Exit (Month 60): $20M acquisition.

| Round | Investor Equity | Dilution | Final Ownership | Exit Value (at $20M) | ROI (on $5,500) |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Strategic ($5,500) | 10% | 50% (seed \+ Series A) | 5% | $1,000,000 | 181x |
| Strategic ($5,500) | 10% | 40% (seed only, no Series A) | 6% | $1,200,000 | 218x |
| Strategic ($5,500) | 10% | 60% (aggressive dilution) | 4% | $800,000 | 145x |

**Conservative ROI (assuming $5M exit, not $20M):** 145x becomes 36x (4% × $5M \= $200,000 / $5,500 \= 36x) – still excellent.

### 22.9 Comparable Strategic Rounds

| Company | Round Size | Valuation | Investor Type | Outcome |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Moniepoint (early) | $10,000 | \~$50,000 | Angel | Now \>$1B valuation |
| Paystack (pre-seed) | $20,000 | \~$100,000 | Angel | Acquired for $200M |
| Flutterwave (seed) | $300,000 | \~$3M | VC | Now \>$3B valuation |
| Cuboid (strategic) | $5,500 | \~$50,000 – $100,000 | Strategic (hands-on) | TBD |

**The pattern:** The most successful Nigerian fintechs raised tiny rounds at absurdly low valuations before exploding. Cuboid is following this playbook.

## SECTION 23: FINANCIAL PROJECTIONS – 3 YEARS – LEAN, BROKER-DRIVEN VOLUME

### 23.1 Overview: Conservative to Optimistic Scenarios

The financial projections below are based on the **moderate scenario** as the baseline, with conservative and optimistic scenarios shown for key metrics. All projections assume no additional funding beyond the initial $5,500 strategic round until Month 12, at which point a seed round of $50,000–$100,000 is raised.

**Key assumptions (moderate scenario):**

| Assumption | Year 1 | Year 2 | Year 3 |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Brokers on platform (end of year) | 500 | 2,000 | 5,000 |
| Active brokers (30-day, % of total) | 60% | 70% | 75% |
| BDCs on platform (end of year) | 50 | 250 | 600 |
| Active BDCs (% of total) | 80% | 85% | 90% |
| Avg monthly volume per active broker | $10,000 | $12,000 | $15,000 |
| Avg monthly volume per active BDC (broker channel) | $50,000 | $60,000 | $80,000 |
| Inter-BDC monthly volume per active BDC | $10,000 | $15,000 | $25,000 |
| Avg transaction fee (broker-BDC) | 0.25% | 0.22% | 0.18% |
| Avg inter-BDC spread | 0.10% | 0.08% | 0.06% |
| BDC subscription avg ($/month) | $35 | $45 | $55 |
| Compliance add-on adoption rate | 40% | 60% | 75% |
| Compliance add-on avg ($/month) | $20 | $22 | $24 |
| API partners (end of year) | 0 | 3 | 10 |
| Avg API monthly fee | $0 | $800 | $1,000 |

### 23.10 Key Financial Ratios (Moderate Scenario)

| Ratio | Year 1 | Year 2 | Year 3 | Industry Benchmark |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Gross Margin | 97% | 98% | 98% | \>80% (excellent) |
| Net Margin | 78% | 71% | 70% | \>20% (excellent) |
| Operating Expense / Revenue | 15% | 18% | 17% | \<50% (efficient) |
| Customer Acquisition Cost (CAC) – BDC | $100 | $120 | $150 | \<$500 (good) |
| Lifetime Value (LTV) – BDC | $5,000 | $6,000 | $8,000 | \>3x CAC (excellent) |
| LTV/CAC Ratio | 50x | 50x | 53x | \>3x (exceptional) |
| Burn Rate (monthly avg) | $2,000 | $10,000 | $25,000 | Very lean |
| Runway (months, no additional revenue) | 60 | 65 | 75 | Extremely healthy |

### 23.11 Break-Even Analysis

| Metric | Value |
| :---- | :---- |
| Monthly fixed costs (Year 1 avg) | $2,000 |
| Average transaction fee revenue per trade | $50 (on $20k avg trade) |
| Trades needed per month to break even | 40 |
| Volume needed per month to break even | $800,000 |
| **Break-even achieved** | **Month 4-5 (conservative)** |

**Explanation:** With 20 active brokers each doing $50,000/month and 5 BDCs each doing $200,000/month, total volume of $1M generates $2,500 in transaction fees (0.25%) – exceeding $2,000 fixed costs. This is achievable by Month 4-5.

### 23.12 Sensitivity Analysis

| Variable | \-20% Change | Baseline | \+20% Change | Impact on Year 2 Net Profit |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Broker-BDC volume | $144M | $180M | $216M | ±$79,200 |
| Avg transaction fee rate | 0.176% | 0.22% | 0.264% | ±$79,200 |
| BDC adoption (end Year 2\) | 200 BDCs | 250 BDCs | 300 BDCs | ±$27,000 |
| Operating expenses | $92,000 | $115,000 | $138,000 | ∓$23,000 |
| **Combined worst case** |  |  |  | **$319,000 (vs baseline $448,200)** |
| **Combined best case** |  |  |  | **$577,000 (vs baseline $448,200)** |

### 23.13 Funding Scenario Comparison

| Scenario | No Seed Round | Seed Round at Month 12 ($100k) | Seed Round \+ Series A (Month 24, $1M) |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Year 2 Revenue | $400,000 | $628,000 | $628,000 |
| Year 3 Revenue | $1,200,000 | $1,812,000 | $3,500,000 |
| Year 3 Net Profit | $600,000 | $1,262,000 | $2,500,000 |
| Founder Dilution (cumulative) | 10% (strategic only) | 25% | 40% |
| Exit Value (at $20M) – Founder | $18M | $15M | $12M |

**Conclusion:** Seed funding accelerates growth but dilutes founders. The optimal path is to raise seed only when organic growth plateaus.

### 23.14 Summary: Financial Projections

| Metric | Year 1 | Year 2 | Year 3 | CAGR |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Volume | $54M | $216M | $744M | 271% |
| Revenue | $152k | $628k | $1.81M | 245% |
| Gross Profit | $147k | $613k | $1.77M | 247% |
| Net Profit | $119k | $448k | $1.26M | 225% |
| Net Margin | 78% | 71% | 70% | – |
| Ending Cash | $121k | $651k | $1.89M | 295% |

**The bottom line:** Cuboid achieves profitability in Year 1, generates $1.8M in revenue and $1.3M in net profit by Year 3, and requires only $5,500 in initial strategic funding plus a modest seed round at Month 12\. The unit economics are exceptional (LTV/CAC \> 50x) and the business model is highly scalable.

## SECTION 24: APPENDICES A & B

### APPENDIX A: DRAFT PARTNER AGREEMENTS (TEMPLATES)

#### A.1 BDC Partner Agreement (Summary)

**Parties:** Cuboid Technologies Ltd. ("Cuboid") and \[BDC Name\] ("Partner BDC")

**Term:** 12 months, automatically renewing unless terminated with 30 days' notice.

**Partner BDC Obligations:**

- Maintain valid CBN BDC license throughout term.  
- Comply with all applicable AML/CFT regulations.  
- File all required CBN/NFIU reports (Cuboid provides tools but does not assume liability).  
- Honor trade requests from brokers accepted through platform.  
- Pay subscription fees and transaction fees as set forth in pricing schedule.

**Cuboid Obligations:**

- Provide access to BDC Management Module.  
- Provide broker demand feed (if enabled).  
- Provide inter-BDC trading functionality.  
- Provide compliance tools (automated filing in Phase 2).  
- Maintain platform availability (99% uptime target).

**Fees (as per Section 21):**

- Subscription: $20–$100 per month based on tier.  
- Transaction fees: 0.15% – 0.3% of trade value.  
- Inter-BDC spread: 0.05% – 0.1% per side.

**Liability:**

- BDC is solely responsible for its own compliance.  
- Cuboid is not liable for BDC's trading losses or compliance failures.  
- BDC indemnifies Cuboid against claims arising from BDC's violation of law.

**Termination:**

- Either party may terminate with 30 days' notice.  
- Cuboid may terminate immediately for BDC's license revocation or material violation of terms.

#### A.2 Broker Terms of Service (Summary – Clickwrap)

**1\. Acceptance of Terms** By registering for Cuboid, you agree to these Terms of Service.

**2\. Prohibition on Unlicensed Trading** You represent and warrant that you will not use Cuboid to engage in any activity that requires a Bureau de Change (BDC) license or other financial services license unless you hold such license. Cuboid is a platform for licensed financial institutions and their authorized partners. Unlicensed FX dealing is prohibited.

**3\. Licensed Counterparty Requirement** All transactions initiated or completed through Cuboid must involve at least one licensed BDC as a counterparty. Broker-to-broker trading is prohibited.

**4\. Audit and Data Access** You acknowledge that all activity on Cuboid is logged and that Cuboid may share these logs with regulatory authorities upon lawful request. You have no expectation of privacy regarding transaction data.

**5\. Compliance Ladder** Cuboid provides tools for customer management, quote generation, and communication. These tools do not constitute legal advice or an exemption from licensing requirements. You are responsible for your own compliance.

**6\. Termination** Cuboid may terminate your access immediately if you violate these terms, including engaging in unlicensed trading or attempting to circumvent the licensed counterparty requirement.

**7\. No Warranties** Cuboid provides the platform "as is" without warranties of merchantability or fitness for a particular purpose.

**8\. Limitation of Liability** Cuboid's liability is limited to the fees paid by you in the preceding 12 months.

#### A.3 Broker-BDC Partnership Agreement (Template)

**Parties:** \[Broker Name\] ("Broker") and \[BDC Name\] ("Sponsor BDC")

**Purpose:** Broker wishes to operate under Sponsor BDC's license for transactions facilitated through Cuboid.

**Term:** 12 months, automatically renewing unless terminated with 30 days' notice.

**Sponsor BDC Obligations:**

- Include Broker's transactions in Sponsor BDC's compliance filings with CBN/NFIU.  
- Ensure Broker has transaction limits appropriate to Broker's verification level.  
- Notify Cuboid if Broker violates terms.

**Broker Obligations:**

- Comply with Sponsor BDC's reasonable policies.  
- Provide customer KYC information to Sponsor BDC upon request.  
- Pay Sponsor BDC a fee of \[0.05% – 0.2%\] of transaction volume (negotiated).

**Fees:**

- Broker pays Sponsor BDC \[X\]% of transaction volume processed under this agreement.  
- Payment made monthly via \[bank transfer / Cuboid settlement\].

**Termination:**

- Either party may terminate with 30 days' notice.  
- Sponsor BDC may terminate immediately if Broker engages in suspicious activity.

**Cuboid's Role:**

- Cuboid is not a party to this agreement.  
- Cuboid will track partnership status and enforce transaction limits accordingly.  
- Cuboid may terminate platform access if partnership is terminated.

#### A.4 Escrow Agreement (Light Escrow – Summary)

**Parties:** Cuboid Technologies Ltd. ("Cuboid"), \[Customer\], \[Broker/BDC\]

**Purpose:** Temporary holding of customer funds pending USD delivery confirmation.

**Escrow Agent:** \[Licensed PSP or bank – to be named in Phase 2; MVP uses manual tracking with Cuboid as facilitator\]

**Escrow Terms:**

- Funds held for maximum 24 hours.  
- Release conditions: (a) USD delivery confirmed by recipient; (b) OR both parties agree to release.  
- Dispute resolution: If parties disagree, escrow agent holds funds for 7 days, then releases based on documentation provided.  
- Cuboid is not a custodian; funds held by licensed third party (Phase 2).

**Fees:** Escrow fee of 0.1% – 0.2% of transaction value, split between parties.

#### B.1 CBN Daily Return Template (Simplified)

**BDC Name:** \[BDC Name\] **License Number:** \[License \#\] **Date:** \[YYYY-MM-DD\]

| Currency | Opening Balance (USD) | Purchases Today (USD) | Sales Today (USD) | Closing Balance (USD) |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| USD | \[amount\] | \[amount\] | \[amount\] | \[amount\] |
| GBP | \[amount\] | \[amount\] | \[amount\] | \[amount\] |
| EUR | \[amount\] | \[amount\] | \[amount\] | \[amount\] |

**Transaction Detail (USD sales \> $500):**

| Customer Name | ID Type | ID Number | Amount (USD) | Exchange Rate | Naira Equivalent | Purpose Code |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| \[name\] | \[NIN/PV/PP\] | \[number\] | \[amount\] | \[rate\] | \[NGN\] | \[P01-P99\] |

**Purpose Codes (CBN standard):**

- P01: School fees  
- P02: Medical expenses  
- P03: Travel (personal)  
- P04: Travel (business)  
- P05: Personal remittances  
- P06: Business imports  
- P99: Other (specify)

**Certification:** I certify that the information above is true and complete.

**Signature:** \_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_\_ (BDC Compliance Officer)

#### B.2 NFIU Currency Transaction Report (CTR) – goAML Format (Simplified)

**Report Type:** Currency Transaction Report (CTR) **Filing Entity:** \[BDC Name\] **License Number:** \[License \#\] **Date of Transaction:** \[YYYY-MM-DD\] **Time of Transaction:** \[HH:MM\]

**Customer Information:**

- Full Name: \[name\]  
- Date of Birth: \[YYYY-MM-DD\]  
- Nationality: Nigerian  
- ID Type: NIN / International Passport / Voter's Card / Driver's License  
- ID Number: \[number\]  
- Address: \[address\]

**Transaction Information:**

- Transaction Type: Currency Exchange  
- Currency From: NGN  
- Currency To: USD  
- Amount From (NGN): \[amount\]  
- Amount To (USD): \[amount\]  
- Exchange Rate: \[rate\]  
- Method of Payment: Bank Transfer / Cash  
- Purpose: \[purpose code \+ description\]  
- Beneficiary (if applicable): \[name\]

**Suspicious Indicators (check if any):**

- [ ] Transaction exceeds customer's profile  
- [ ] Structuring suspected (multiple transactions just below threshold)  
- [ ] Unusual geographic pattern  
- [ ] Customer unable to explain source of funds  
- [ ] Other: \[describe\]

**Filing Officer:** \[name\] **Contact:** \[phone\]

#### B.3 Suspicious Transaction Report (STR) – goAML Format (Simplified)

**Report Type:** Suspicious Transaction Report (STR) **Filing Entity:** \[BDC Name\] **Date of Report:** \[YYYY-MM-DD\]

**Subject Information:**

- Full Name: \[name\]  
- Known Aliases: \[if any\]  
- Date of Birth: \[YYYY-MM-DD\]  
- Address: \[address\]  
- Occupation: \[occupation\]  
- Phone Number: \[phone\]

**Suspicious Activity Description:**

- Date(s) of Activity: \[date range\]  
- Transaction Amount(s): \[amounts\]  
- Currency: USD / NGN  
- Description of Suspicious Activity: \[detailed description\]  
- Red Flags Observed: \[list\]

**Supporting Evidence:**

- [ ] Transaction logs attached  
- [ ] Customer communication attached  
- [ ] KYC documents attached

**Filing Officer:** \[name\] **Contact:** \[phone\]

**Internal Reference Number:** \[Cuboid-generated\]

**Note to BDC:** This STR must be filed with NFIU within 24 hours of suspicion. Cuboid provides this template but BDC is responsible for submission.

#### B.4 Regulator Dashboard – Sample Data View (Anonymized)

**Cuboid Platform – Monthly Activity Report (Anonymized)** **Reporting Period:** \[Month, Year\]

**Summary:**

- Total platform volume: $XX,XXX,XXX  
- Number of active BDCs: XX  
- Number of active brokers: XXX  
- Number of customer transactions: X,XXX

**Volume by Geographic Region:**

## SECTION 25: APPENDICES C, D, & E

### APPENDIX C: USER JOURNEY MAPS

#### C.1 Broker User Journey (Rung 2 → Rung 3 → Rung 4\)

**Phase 1: Discovery & Signup (Rung 2\)**

| Step | Touchpoint | User Action | System Response | Emotions |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | WhatsApp referral | Receives message: "Try Cuboid – faster than calling" | N/A | Curious, skeptical |
| 2 | Website landing page | Clicks link, sees "FX productivity tool" | Loads mobile-optimized page | Intrigued |
| 3 | Signup form | Enters phone number | Sends OTP via SMS/WhatsApp | Cautious |
| 4 | OTP verification | Enters OTP | Creates account, shows dashboard | Relieved (easy) |
| 5 | Tutorial (optional) | Skips or watches 30-second video | Dashboard loads with chat interface | Overwhelmed (slight) |

**Phase 2: First Trade Request**

| Step | Touchpoint | User Action | System Response | Emotions |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | Chat interface | Types "need $5k USD for school fees" | NLP parses request | Hopeful |
| 2 | BDC inventory feed | Shows 3 BDCs with rates, distances | Displays options | Surprised (fast) |
| 3 | Select BDC | Taps "Request" on preferred BDC | Sends trade request to BDC | Satisfied |
| 4 | Wait for response | Waits (typical 1-3 minutes) | Shows "pending" status | Anxious |
| 5 | BDC accepts | Receives notification "BDC accepted" | Confirms trade, locks inventory | Relieved, pleased |
| 6 | Settlement | Customer sends naira, broker confirms | Tracks settlement status | Focused |
| 7 | Completion | BDC confirms USD delivery | Marks trade complete, logs receipt | Accomplished |

**Phase 3: First Week of Usage**

| Day | Activity | User Behavior | System Engagement | Retention Risk |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | Explore features | Tries quote generator, adds 5 customers | Shows tips, nudges | Low |
| 2 | Second trade | Uses chat-to-trade again | Faster response | Low |
| 3 | Customer management | Adds 10 more customers | Suggests "you have 15 customers" | Low |
| 4 | Daily habit | Checks inventory feed in morning | Shows daily summary | Very low |
| 5 | Referral | Tells another broker about Cuboid | None (organic) | Low |
| 7 | Retention | Still active after 7 days | "Week 1 complete" message | Moderate (converted) |

**Phase 4: Upgrading to Rung 3 (ID Verification)**

| Step | Touchpoint | User Action | System Response | Emotions |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | Nudge | Receives: "Verify ID to unlock escrow" | After 10 trade requests | Considerate |
| 2 | Verification screen | Clicks "Verify Now" | Opens Smile ID widget | Cautious (privacy) |
| 3 | ID upload | Takes photo of NIN or passport | Validates document | Anxious (data sharing) |
| 4 | Selfie | Takes live selfie | Matches with ID | Slightly uncomfortable |
| 5 | Processing (30 sec) | Waits | Shows "verifying..." | Antsy |
| 6 | Verified | "Verification successful" | Upgrades to Rung 3 | Relieved, proud |
| 7 | First escrow trade | Uses escrow for $10k trade | Holds customer funds | Confident |

**Phase 5: Upgrading to Rung 4 (Partnering with BDC)**

| Step | Touchpoint | User Action | System Response | Emotions |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | Nudge | "You've done 50 trades. Partner with a BDC." | After $250k cumulative volume | Interested |
| 2 | Partnership offer | Reviews partner BDC options | Shows 5 BDCs accepting partners | Excited |
| 3 | Select BDC | Taps "Partner" on preferred BDC | Sends partnership request | Hopeful |
| 4 | BDC reviews | Waits (1-2 days) | Status: "Pending BDC approval" | Anxious |
| 5 | Approved | "Your partnership with \[BDC\] is active" | Upgrades to Rung 4 | Proud, relieved |
| 6 | Increased limits | Sees higher transaction limits | Dashboard shows new limits | Empowered |
| 7 | Long-term retention | Continues trading with compliance coverage | Persistent user | Loyal |

   |   skeptical)         relieved)          proud)            loyal)

   |  😕 → 😊 → 😌 → 😐 → 😬 → 😌 → 😊 → 😎

#### C.2 BDC User Journey (Rung 5 – Licensed BDC)

| 4 | Receipt generation | Issues first digital receipt | QR code generated | Satisfied |
| 5 | Inter-BDC trading | Posts excess USD, finds buyer | Matches with deficit BDC | Pleased |
| 7 | Broker demand feed | Sees 5 broker requests, accepts 3 | New revenue channel | Converted |

| 2 | Broker volume growth | Sees $100k from brokers | Broker demand feed | Very low |
| 3 | Inter-BDC trading | Balances inventory, reduces idle USD | Matches daily | Very low |
| 4 | Subscription renewal | Auto-renews | Payment processed | Low |
| 8 | Compliance add-on (Phase 2\) | Enables one-click filing | Auto-generates reports | Very low (locked in) |
| 12 | Referral | Refers another BDC | Earns referral credit | Loyal |

#### C.3 Regulator User Journey (Dashboard Access – Phase 3\)

| Step | Touchpoint | Regulator Action | System Response | Outcome |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| 1 | Initial meeting (Month 6\) | Cuboid presents platform to CBN Fintech Desk | Demo dashboard | Interest |
| 2 | Follow-up (Month 7\) | Regulator requests more data | Cuboid provides anonymized volume, trends | Engagement |
| 3 | Sandbox application (Month 8\) | CBN reviews application | Formal acknowledgment | Pending |
| 4 | Dashboard access (Month 9\) | CBN grants sandbox approval, requests read-only access | Cuboid creates regulator account | Visibility |
| 5 | Monthly review | Regulator views dashboard: volume, BDC compliance | Automated report email | Trust building |
| 6 | Formal MOU (Month 12\) | CBN/NFIU signs data sharing agreement | API integration begins | Partnership |
| 7 | Ongoing (Month 12+) | Regulator uses Cuboid data for policy decisions | Real-time insights | Strategic value |

### APPENDIX D: COMPETITOR ANALYSIS – INCLUDES INFORMAL CHANNELS

#### D.1 Competitive Landscape Overview

| Competitor | Type | Target User | Broker Awareness | Cuboid Advantage |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| **WhatsApp/Phone (Informal)** | Communication | Brokers, BDCs | High (they use it) | Adds inventory visibility, escrow, customer mgmt |
| **Excel/Paper (Manual)** | Record keeping | BDCs | None | Automation, compliance, network effects |
| **FMDQ (Formal FX Exchange)** | Institutional trading | Banks, large corporates | None | Retail focus, BDC/broker friendly |
| **Bank-provided portals** | Reporting only | BDCs | None | BDC-owned, not bank-dependent |
| **Custom software (Finacle, etc.)** | BDC management | Enterprise BDCs | None | 1/10th cost, network effects |
| **Competitor fintechs (Chipper, etc.)** | Consumer FX | End users | None (bypass BDCs) | BDC-friendly, regulatory defensible |
| **Informal broker networks (Telegram, etc.)** | Communication | Brokers | High | Adds structure, trust scoring, escrow |

#### D.2 Detailed Competitor Analysis

**D.2.1 WhatsApp / Phone (Primary Competitor)**

| Aspect | Details |
| :---- | :---- |
| Current usage | 90%+ of brokers use WhatsApp for sourcing, quoting, settlement |
| Strengths | Free, familiar, instant, no learning curve |
| Weaknesses | No inventory visibility (must call each contact), no escrow, no audit trail, no customer management |
| Why users stay | "It's what everyone uses" – network effects |
| Cuboid response | Same familiar chat interface, but with inventory feed, escrow, customer mgmt built in |

**D.2.2 Excel / Paper (BDC Status Quo)**

| Aspect | Details |
| :---- | :---- |
| Current usage | \~90% of BDCs use Excel or paper for inventory, receipts |
| Strengths | Free (except labor), flexible |
| Weaknesses | Manual entry errors, no real-time visibility, no compliance automation, no inter-BDC trading |
| Why users stay | "We've always done it this way" – inertia |
| Cuboid response | Low-cost ($20-100/month) digital solution with 18x ROI |

**D.2.3 FMDQ (Formal FX Exchange)**

| Aspect | Details |
| :---- | :---- |
| Focus | Wholesale FX, institutional trading, banks |
| Strengths | Regulator-approved, transparent, high volume |
| Weaknesses | Not retail, not BDC/broker friendly, high barriers to entry |
| Cuboid response | Cuboid serves retail segment that FMDQ ignores |

**D.2.4 Bank-Provided Portals**

| Aspect | Details |
| :---- | :---- |
| Examples | GTBank BDC portal, Access Bank BDC reporting |
| Focus | Compliance reporting only (CBN daily returns) |
| Strengths | Free, bank-approved |
| Weaknesses | No trading, no inventory, no inter-BDC, bank-specific (BDC must have account) |
| Cuboid response | BDC-agnostic, full management \+ trading \+ compliance |

**D.2.5 Custom Software (Finacle, etc.)**

| Aspect | Details |
| :---- | :---- |
| Examples | Finacle BDC solution, other ERP modules |
| Focus | Enterprise BDCs with \>10 branches |
| Strengths | Feature-rich, customizable |
| Weaknesses | Expensive ($5k+ upfront \+ $500/month), no network effects, no broker integration |
| Cuboid response | 1/10th cost, includes network (broker feed, inter-BDC trading) |

**D.2.6 Consumer-Facing Fintechs (Chipper, etc.)**

| Aspect | Details |
| :---- | :---- |
| Examples | Chipper Cash FX, Bamboo, Risevest (some have FX features) |
| Focus | End users (consumers) – bypass BDCs entirely |
| Strengths | Convenient for tech-savvy users |
| Weaknesses | Regulatory risk (operating without BDC license), limited scale, no BDC partnership |
| Cuboid response | Partner with BDCs, not bypass them – regulator-friendly |

**D.2.7 Informal Broker Networks (Telegram, WhatsApp Groups)**

| Aspect | Details |
| :---- | :---- |
| Examples | Private Telegram groups, WhatsApp broadcast lists |
| Focus | Brokers only |
| Strengths | Free, large networks |
| Weaknesses | No tools, no trust scoring, high scam risk, no dispute resolution |
| Cuboid response | Adds structure, trust scoring, escrow, while keeping chat interface |

#### D.3 Cuboid Competitive Positioning Matrix

| Feature | WhatsApp | Excel | Bank Portal | Custom Software | Fintech Apps | Cuboid |
| :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- | :---- |
| Chat interface | ✓ | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✓ |
| Inventory visibility | ✗ | ✓ (manual) | ✗ | ✓ | ✗ | ✓ (real-time) |
| Quote generation | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✓ | ✓ |
| Customer management | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✓ | ✓ | ✓ |
| Digital receipts | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✓ | ✗ | ✓ |
| Inter-BDC trading | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✓ |
| Broker demand feed | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✓ |
| Compliance automation | ✗ | ✗ | ✓ (basic) | ✓ | ✗ | ✓ (Phase 2\) |
| Escrow / settlement | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✓ (light) |
| Audit trail | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✓ | ✗ | ✓ |
| Low cost (\<$100/month) | ✓ | ✓ | ✓ | ✗ | ✓ | ✓ |
| Network effects | ✓ | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ | ✓ |

#### D.4 SWOT Analysis (Cuboid vs Informal Channels)

**Strengths:**

- Addresses real broker pain points (inventory discovery, settlement risk)  
- Familiar chat interface reduces learning curve  
- Extremely low cost ($0 for brokers, $20-100 for BDCs)  
- Built on Insane Technologies infrastructure (reduces dev cost)

**Weaknesses:**

- No brand recognition (new entrant)  
- Network effects of WhatsApp (everyone already there)  
- Brokers may be reluctant to adopt new tool  
- Regulatory risk (perceived legitimization of brokers)

**Opportunities:**

- 90%+ of brokers have no digital tool – huge greenfield  
- CBN reforms create urgency for BDCs to digitize  
- Banks and fintechs need BDC network – API opportunity  
- Broker referral program creates viral growth

**Threats:**

- CBN could shut down platform if perceived as facilitating unlicensed trading  
- WhatsApp could build similar features (unlikely – not their focus)  
- A competitor could copy Cuboid's model (requires broker network, hard to replicate)

| R-07 | Market | Competitor launches similar product with more funding | Medium | Medium | Medium | Move fast; Insane Technologies infrastructure advantage; network lock-in | Founder |
| R-08 | Operational | Founder burnout (single point of failure) | Medium | High | High | Document processes; train backup; Phase 4 hires | Founder |
| R-09 | Operational | Settlement dispute escalates to legal action | Low | Medium | Low | Clear terms; escrow for high-value trades | Legal |
| R-10 | Operational | BDC churn due to poor support | Medium | Medium | Medium | Dedicated BDC contact; proactive check-ins | Sales |
| R-11 | Operational | Broker churn due to complexity | Medium | Medium | Medium | Simplify UX; video tutorials; WhatsApp support | Product |

| R-13 | Technical | Database failure / data loss | Low | High | Medium | Automated backups; multi-region replication | Development |
| R-14 | Technical | Chat infrastructure cannot scale | Low | Medium | Low | Use managed WebSocket service (e.g., Pusher) | Development |
| R-15 | Financial | Insufficient funding before revenue | Low | High | Medium | Lean operations; $5,500 covers 12 months; revenue from Month 4 | Founder |
| R-16 | Financial | Revenue growth slower than projected | Medium | Medium | Medium | Conservative projections; multiple revenue streams | Founder |
| R-17 | Legal | Data privacy violation (NDPR) | Low | High | Medium | Data processing agreements; limited data collection; user consent | Legal |
| R-18 | Legal | Insane Technologies equity dispute | Low | High | Medium | Clear shareholders' agreement; vesting schedule | Legal |
| R-19 | Legal | Founder departure | Low | High | Medium | Vesting schedule; IP assignment agreement | Legal |
| R-20 | Reputational | Media exposé on "broker platform" | Low | Medium | Low | Proactive transparency; invite media to review compliance | Founder |
